A Creative Commons license covers **copyrightable content**. It is not a trademark license and not a certification. Specifically:

1. **Names and marks are not licensed here.** "Possibility Management," "Possibilitator," "StartOver.xyz," the SPARK / matrix-code system, and related names and logos belong to their holders. CC BY-SA 4.0 explicitly does **not** grant trademark rights. If you use those names, follow Possibility Management's own guidelines for them — for example, do not present your offering as an official Possibility Management training or certification unless you actually hold that standing.
2. **Releasing this open does not, by itself, make it "official PM."** This course is an independent, good-faith re-presentation of openly-licensed PM thoughtware. Open-copyleft release is consistent with PM's own ShareAlike terms (you are required to share derivatives alike — which is exactly what this does). It is not the same thing as endorsement, certification, or sponsorship by Clinton Callahan or the Possibility Management organization.
3. **The safety, intake, and clinical-referral material is content, not professional advice.** The license does not transfer any duty of care, professional qualification, or legal compliance to a downstream user. If you run a cohort, the obligations in `03 - Safety and Facilitation Framework.md` and `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` — and applicable law on health-data handling, duty of care, and your jurisdiction's rules — are yours to meet. See those documents and, where relevant, get your own legal and clinical counsel.

In short: **the thoughtware is open — please share it and build on it. The marks, the standing, and the responsibilities are not handed over with the text.**

# §  START HERE (Learner Welcome)

***

# Start Here

*Read this once before you open Day 1. It's the only orientation you need. Fifteen minutes.*

Welcome to Expand the Box. This page tells you how the course actually works — the rhythm, the people, the safety net, and what to do on your first day. The Day modules teach Possibility Management. This page teaches you how to *take* the course.

---

## What this is, in one breath

Ten modules over about thirty days. You watch short videos, read a tightly-written module, do one solo practice, exchange a voice message with one partner, run one small experiment in your actual life, and write a few reflections. Then you do it again, nine more times. The work is not in the watching. It's in the practices and the experiments — the small reps you run between the videos.

It is **not** therapy, coaching, or treatment. It is an education in a set of distinctions and maps. It will sometimes be uncomfortable — that's the work — but discomfort that overwhelms you is your cue to pause and reach for support, not to push through. More on that below.

---

## The rhythm of one module

You move through one module every **~3 days**. There's no clock forcing you; this is the shape that works:

- **Day one of the cycle:** watch the module's video(s), read the module, do the solo practice (~2 hours on lighter days, ~3 on the heavier ones — each module's header tells you its real time).
- **Across the next day or two:** run the *between-module experiment* — a small specific rep you do inside your ordinary life (a conversation you were going to have anyway, a meeting, dinner). It costs no extra scheduled time.
- **Before the next module:** send your partner a voice message, listen to theirs, write your reflections, post one line to the cohort feed.

Faster is fine (≈20 days). Slower is fine (≈60). What matters is the rhythm — *content → practice → experiment → reflection* — not the speed.

---

## The intensity tags

Every module is tagged **Low**, **Medium**, or **High**. The tag is in the module header and it's honest about what the day asks of you.

- **Low** (Days 1, 3, 4, 10): mostly cognitive and embodied-light. *One exception:* **Day 3 is Low emotional intensity but it is load-bearing** — it installs the centering, grounding, and bubble practices that every hard day later stands on. Don't skim Day 3.
- **Medium** (Days 2, 8): real but manageable charge.
- **High** (Days 5, 6, 7, 9): these directly engage your feelings, your drama patterns, and your shadow. They can surface material you haven't met before. They require an active partner and a consent check before you begin. Take them when you have time, privacy, and your partner is reachable — not at the end of a hard day.

The three High modules in a row — **Days 5, 6, 7** — are the heaviest stretch of the course. There's a built-in integration pause between Day 6 and Day 7. Use it. Don't power through.

---

## The four agreements

Beginning Day 1 means agreeing to four things. They're repeated at the top of each module. They are what make the work safe.

1. **Choice is always available.** You can pause, skip a practice, slow down, take a longer break, or stop entirely. Nothing here is mandatory. No part of this course requires you to push through anything. If your body says no, the answer is no.
2. **Consent is ongoing.** Each High module asks your consent again before it begins. Agreeing once at enrollment doesn't carry forward into every exercise. You can decline any single practice and keep going.
3. **You are responsible for your own state.** The course gives you the practices — center, ground, drop a bubble, feel, choose. You use them. If you can't reach them in a moment, you pause and reach for support.
4. **Your partner is alive.** Before the High modules (5, 6, 7, 9), you confirm your partner is reachable. If they're not, the module waits. This isn't a suggestion — it's the structure.

---

## Your partner

You'll be matched with one other learner for the whole course. You exchange voice messages — usually 3–8 minutes each way, once per module. They are your witness, not your therapist, coach, or fixer. What they do: listen, reflect back what they actually heard, ask you one open question. What they don't do: advise, diagnose, or fix.

You don't need to be good at this yet — the course teaches the listening and speaking on Day 8. Until then, "I heard you say… here's what moved in me… here's one question I'm leaving with you" is enough.

**If your partner goes quiet:** tell your community manager (see below). There's a real fallback — a witness partner or a CM-held exchange — so a silent partner never strands you. You don't have to solve it alone, and you don't have to wait indefinitely.

---

## The cohort feed

A shared space where everyone posts a line or two after each module — what landed, what's sticking sideways, an optional question. Keep it brief; the deep processing goes to your partner, not the feed. Don't post other people's stories. Don't give advice. It's a place to be witnessed by the group, lightly.

---

## Your community manager (CM)

One person holds the container for your cohort. They're reachable by message — within 24 hours for ordinary things, **immediately** for anything urgent. Reach the CM when: your partner isn't working, something in your life changed that affects whether you should continue, you want a referral, or you're worried about yourself or someone else in the cohort.

The CM is not your therapist. They keep the container intact and point you to the right support. That's a real and skilled job — it's just not clinical care.

---

## When it gets to be too much

This is the part to read twice.

**The 60-second grounding practice** — use it any time you notice you're floating, can't follow the words, your heart is racing without cause, you're watching yourself from outside, or you have a strong urge to flee, attack, or shut down:

> 1. Stop. Close the video or the page.
> 2. Stand up. Both feet on the floor. Knees soft.
> 3. Breathe out longer than you breathe in — three times. Out loud is fine.
> 4. Name three things you can see.
> 5. Name one thing you can hear.
> 6. One hand on your chest, one on your belly. Notice your body is here.
> 7. Then decide: continue, pause ten minutes, or stop for today.

The interactive tools on the High days have a **GROUND NOW** button that opens this script with one tap. The script lives at the top of every module too.

**Three levels of "this is hard":**
- Discomfort that is *moving* → keep going gently. This is the work.
- Discomfort that is *stuck or escalating* → ground, pause at least ten minutes, then re-decide.
- Discomfort that is *unmistakably crisis* → stop, contact your partner, and if needed the referral list. If you or someone else may be in immediate danger, contact local emergency services or your country's crisis line **now** — don't wait for the course.

You received a **referral packet** when you enrolled — crisis lines, clinicians, and coaches for your region. Keep it somewhere you can reach in thirty seconds. If you don't have it, ask your CM before you start Day 1.

**This course is not a substitute for therapy or medical care.** If what surfaces is bigger than a thoughtware course is built to hold, that's not you doing it wrong — it's the signal to bring in someone qualified. The course will still be here.

---

## A few words you'll meet on Day 1

You don't need to study these — they're taught as you go. Just so they're not strangers:

- **The Box** — the survival-and-protection thoughtware you assembled as a kid. The whole course turns on one line: *you have a Box, you are not your Box.*
- **Thoughtware** — what you think *with* (the operating system), as distinct from what you think *about*.
- **Liquid state** — the loosened state in which thoughtware can actually change.
- **Gremlin** — the part of you that feeds on drama. Met directly later.
- **Beep! Book** — a literal notebook you'll start on Day 4 as your engineering log of small experiments. Have a notebook ready.
- **Experiment** — a small, specific, real-life rep with a clear *what I'll do / by when / what I'll notice*. The reps compound.

---

## Before you open Day 1, check:

- [ ] You've been matched with a partner (or your CM is matching you).
- [ ] You have your region's referral packet within reach.
- [ ] You know how to message your CM.
- [ ] You have a notebook for your reflections and (from Day 4) your Beep! Book.
- [ ] You have ~90 uninterrupted minutes for the module itself.

That's everything. When you're ready, open **Day 1 — Orientation, New Context, Radical Responsibility**. It starts by asking you to choose, on purpose, to be here.

Welcome in.

---

# §  README (operator)

***

# Expand the Box — Async Online Course

A 10-module, self-paced online course in **Possibility Management** — the body of thoughtware developed by Clinton Callahan and the PM community.

This folder contains the complete course: architecture, frameworks, ten self-contained modules (each teaching its maps inline), twenty-nine Map Note cards, a `Maps/` image set, a `Map Atlas/` of 29 interactive map tools, facilitator resources, and a single-file assembled version.

---

## License — World Copyleft 🄯 (open, anyone can use)

**This whole course is released under [Creative Commons Attribution-ShareAlike 4.0 (CC BY-SA 4.0)](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0/)** — the same "World Copyleft" terms Possibility Management uses for its Sparks and maps. You are free to **share, adapt, translate, run cohorts on it, and use it commercially** — provided you (1) **attribute** the lineage (*Possibility Management thoughtware originated by Clinton Callahan and the PM community; this course is a derivative re-presentation*), (2) license your derivatives under the **same** CC BY-SA 4.0 (share-alike), and (3) indicate changes.

What's open is the *content* (text, Map Notes, the rendered maps, the interactive tools). What is **not** handed over: the names and marks ("Possibility Management," "Possibilitator," "StartOver.xyz"), any endorsement/certification standing, and the safety/legal responsibilities of actually running a cohort. **Full terms, scope, and the honest caveats are in [`LICENSE.md`](LICENSE.md) — read it before redistributing or selling.**

*Powered by Possibility Management — [possibilitymanagement.org](https://possibilitymanagement.org). Experimenting builds matrix to hold more consciousness. Please share.*

---

## What this course is for

A learner who wants their thoughtware upgraded. Specifically:
- The Box becomes visible enough that the learner can disidentify from it
- The four feelings (anger, sadness, fear, joy) become distinct, useful, archetypal energies rather than "things to manage"
- The Low Drama Triangle becomes detectable in real time
- Listening and speaking become acts of possibility, not transmission
- The three powers — choosing, asking dangerous questions, declaring — become operational

The course does this through 10 self-paced modules, async partner pairings, embodied practices, between-module experiments, and a structured safety container.

The course is **not** therapy. Not coaching. Not trauma treatment. Not psychiatric care. It is an educational course in PM thoughtware. See `03 - Safety and Facilitation Framework.md` for the full distinction.

---

---

## Reading order

### For a learner about to take the course
**Read `00 - START HERE (Learner Welcome).md` — that one page is your whole orientation** (how the course works, the agreements, the grounding practice, what to do if it gets to be too much). You do **not** need to read this README or the operator docs. Then, with your community manager:
1. Read `00 - START HERE (Learner Welcome).md` (≈15 min)
2. Complete intake screening (your CM sends it)
3. Confirm you have your region's referral packet
4. Get paired with a partner
5. Open `Days/Day 01 …`

*(Sections B, C, D, F, I of `03 - Safety and Facilitation Framework.md` are the operator's source for the safety practices; the Start-Here page already assembles what a learner needs from them, in learner voice.)*

### For a community manager preparing to run a cohort
1. Read this README in full
2. Read `01 - Course Architecture and Pedagogy.md` in full
3. Read `02 - Async Delivery Framework.md` in full
4. Read `03 - Safety and Facilitation Framework.md` cover to cover
5. Read **`04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` in full — this is the operational protocol; the cohort cannot open without it**
6. Read `Facilitator Resources/Async Partner Pairing Playbook.md` and `Cohort Feed Templates.md`
7. Skim Day 1, Day 5, Day 10 to understand the arc
8. Complete the pre-cohort checklist (Doc 04 Section K)
9. Open the cohort

### For a course designer or contributor
1. Read 00 (Source Inventory) — what the course was built from
2. Read 01 (Architecture) — why the course is shaped the way it is, especially the "Key distinctions baked into the architecture" section
3. Read the locked templates in 01 (Module shape, Map Note shape)
4. Read Day 1, Day 5, Day 10 as voice anchors
5. Skim a few Map Notes (M01, M10, M13, M23 cover the range)
6. Then contribute

---

## Course architecture in one glance

| Phase | Modules | What gets installed |
|---|---|---|
| **Container & frame** | 1, 2 | New context · the chain · the Box as filter · radical responsibility |
| **Embodiment infrastructure** | 3, 4 | Liquid state · center/ground/bubble · five bodies · feedback · coaching · experiments |
| **Emotional body** | 5, 6 | Feelings vs emotions · old map · numbness bar · mixed emotions · emotional healing process |
| **Relational body** | 7, 8 | Low Drama · gremlin food · listening · speaking · completion loops |
| **Integration** | 9, 10 | Ego states · problem ownership · learning spiral · map of possibility · bright principles · three powers |

Each module is one file in `Days/`. Each module follows a 14-section locked template (header → purpose → core concepts → learning outcomes → maps → flow → teaching notes → embodied practice → partner exchange → between-module experiment → reflection prompts → safety callouts → cohort feed post → glossary additions).

Each map has a one-page **Map Note card** in `Map Notes/` (29 in total) — the embedded ETB map, a short "what it is / at a glance" summary, and links to its day module and its interactive **Map Atlas** tool. The full teaching now lives in the day modules (where each map is taught inline) and in the Map Atlas. M01–M23 follow the day arc; M24–M29 are supplementary maps wired into the days they support (Day 1, 4, 7, 9, 10).

---

## The Map Atlas

`Map Atlas/` holds 29 standalone interactive map-teaching tools — one per map, M01 through M29 — opened from `Map Atlas/index.html`. Each tool walks the learner through a single map in the browser, made clickable and self-paced rather than only read. It is the interactive companion to the Day modules and to the slimmed-down Map Note cards, so a learner can either read a map or work through it. The Day pages under `Interactive Tools/` link straight to the matching Atlas tool for every map they install.

---

## Pacing

The default cadence is **one module per ~3 days, ~30 days total**. See `02 - Async Delivery Framework.md` Section I for cadence variants. The course is async; the learner sets the pace within their cohort's container.

---

## Safety, in one sentence

The container is real, the safety practices are explicit, the screening is the gate (not a recommendation), the partner pairing is structural, the referral pathway is one click away from any module, and the course does not pretend to be appropriate for everyone. See `03` and `04` for the full structure.

---

## Provenance and lineage

All Possibility Management distinctions in this course originate with Clinton Callahan and the PM community since the late 1980s. The course **does not** reproduce source videos, transcripts, or photographed maps from the source library — it re-presents the distinctions in clean facilitator language for async delivery. If this course is ever distributed externally, the lineage attribution must travel with it.

Lineage source material used to reconstruct the course distinctions (read-only during course design):
- ETB Online January 2026 recorded cohort: **18 available concept lecture videos in a 19-slot canonical sequence** (slot 08 is missing — Day 4 is reconstructed from Sparks + transcripts + book), 11 live session transcripts, 22 handwritten maps
- Conscious Feelings by Clinton Callahan
- 258 PM Sparks
- The Periodic Table of Possibility Management Distinctions
- Live training maps from Possibility Lab NY (October 2025), Youtopia (June 2025), Upstate NY (May 2025)

See `00 - Source Inventory and Concept Coverage Matrix.md` for the full inventory and the concept-to-source mapping.

---

## A note on what's deliberately left out

- No badges, streaks, completion certificates, or gamification — PM does not reward compliance
- No replay-able quizzes — PM is verified in lived experience
- No public discussion forum for "questions about PM" — that conversation happens elsewhere; the cohort feed stays narrow
- No app — a platform is enough

The course's force is in the modules, the partner pairings, and the experiments the learner runs in their actual life. Everything else is infrastructure.

---

## Versioning

**Course version 1.0** — first complete draft. The locked templates (Module shape, Map Note shape) and the four working agreements cannot change mid-cohort; only between full cohort runs. Individual module content and Map Note content can be revised continuously as the course is used and the post-cohort reviews (Doc 04 Section L) surface patterns.

# §  00 — Source Inventory and Concept Coverage Matrix

***

# 00 — Source Inventory and Concept Coverage Matrix

**Purpose.** This document maps every Possibility Management concept the course teaches to the source material it draws on. It is the audit trail for the course design and the first place a future facilitator should look when checking whether a distinction was reconstructed faithfully.

**Source treatment.** All source folders are read-only. The course was written by *reading* the source material as inspiration — never by copying, moving, editing, or unzipping it.

---

## A. Primary Source Folder — `ETB Online January 2026/`

This is the recorded January 2026 cohort. It contains the live audio sessions, the 19 numbered concept lecture videos, and the handwritten maps photographed during the live training.

### A.1 Concept lecture videos (19 numbered)

The numbering corresponds to the canonical ETB teaching sequence. Each video is one self-contained concept lecture.

| # | Title (as on disk) | Concept |
|---|---|---|
| 01 | `01 - New Context_EN.mp4` | The chain: new context → new thoughtmaps → new options → new choices → new behavior → new results |
| 02 | `02 - New Responsibility & Culture.mp4` (+ `.MOV`) | Radical responsibility and the cultural shift from victim to creator |
| 03 | `03 - Map Of Thoughtware.mp4` (+ `.mov`) | What "thoughtware" is and why upgrading it is the work |
| 04 | `04 - MapOfThoughtmaps_EN.mp4` | What a thoughtmap is and how PM maps function as cognitive tools |
| 05 | `05 - BoxTechnology_EN.mp4` | The Box as survival/protection filter; "you have a box, you are not your box" |
| 06 | `06 - LiquidState_EN.mp4` | Liquid state as the gateway for change |
| 07 | `07 - 5Bodies_EN.mp4` (+ `5Bodies En.mp4`) | Intellectual / emotional / physical / energetic / archetypal bodies |

## E. Provenance Note

Every map photographed by hand in the source folder belongs to the **lineage of Clinton Callahan and the Possibility Management community**. The course rewrites those distinctions in clean facilitator language — it does not reproduce the photographs or transcribe the videos. Where a Map Note refers a learner to a visual, it points back to the read-only source path. If this course is ever distributed externally, the maps and lineage attribution must be carried with it.

# §  01 — Course Architecture and Pedagogy

***

# 01 — Course Architecture and Pedagogy

## What this course is

**Expand the Box** is a ten-module, self-paced online course that teaches the core thoughtware of **Possibility Management (PM)** — the body of distinctions, maps and practices developed by Clinton Callahan and the PM community since the late 1980s.

It is a **thoughtware upgrade**. The learner's Box — the survival-and-protection thoughtware they have been identified with — becomes visible enough that they can disidentify from it, enter liquid state, choose a new context, and run experiments from there. The course is not "self-improvement"; it is an apprenticeship in catching the Box in the act and choosing differently while it is happening.

It is **not** therapy. It is not coaching. It is not a workshop with prepackaged "techniques." It is an apprenticeship in noticing — supported by maps, distinctions, embodied practices, partner pairings, and structured between-module experiments.

---

## The pedagogical premise

PM rests on a single load-bearing claim:

> What you are able to think with determines what becomes possible to choose, feel, speak and create. Upgrading thoughtware is therefore upstream of any change in behavior, relationship, or what life can become.

Everything in this course follows from that. Specifically:

1. **Maps before practice.** A learner who tries to "do anger differently" without a new map of feelings will reproduce the old map's habits in slightly different costume. So each module installs the relevant map *first*, then asks the learner to live inside it.
2. **Distinctions before techniques.** PM does not give "techniques" the learner masters. It gives **distinctions** the learner uses. A distinction is a perceptual cut — once seen, it changes what's available without requiring any "skill." Examples: *feeling vs. emotion*; *box vs. you*; *low drama vs. responsible game*; *is-glue vs. has-glue*.
3. **Five-body learning.** Cognitive content alone reinstalls the box. Each module engages at least three of the five bodies — intellectual, emotional, physical, energetic, archetypal — so the learning lands in the place where new behavior actually originates.
4. **Practice in the small.** New choices stabilize through small experiments in which the learner catches the Box in the act and chooses from Adult (or radical) instead. The course's "experiments" are often a single sentence said in a single conversation. Not a transformation. A rep. The reps compound.
5. **No authority transfer.** PM is structurally designed to *not* make the facilitator the source of the learner's knowing. The course mirrors this: prompts ask the learner to verify each distinction in their own direct experience, not to take the facilitator's word.

---

## Key distinctions baked into the architecture

Seven distinctions sit underneath every module. They are not always named explicitly in the modules themselves — they are the architecture the modules assume. Anyone designing, adapting, or co-facilitating this course needs to be able to hold them.

### 1. Context (the proper PM definition)

In ordinary usage "context" means surroundings or background. **In PM, context is the invisible source-frame that determines what actions, meanings, choices, and results are even available.** It is upstream of mindset, beliefs, and intentions. Two people in the same content can be in radically different contexts and produce radically different results.

The course's whole machinery — the chain (context → thoughtware → thoughtmaps → options → choices → behavior → results) — runs on the premise that the leftmost link is the most leveraged and the most invisible. Most learners arrive trying to change their behavior. The course works on context.

### 2. Possibility paradigm vs causal paradigm

The **causal paradigm** explains what is happening by reference to the past: "I am like this because of my childhood / my trauma / my conditioning." It is descriptively useful and developmentally honest. It is also a closed loop — every present moment is sourced from a fixed past.

The **possibility paradigm** creates what becomes by reference to a chosen context and a created future. It does not deny the past; it relocates the source of action from past-as-cause to context-as-source. The course does not ask the learner to abandon causal explanation. It asks them to spend 10 modules treating context as the more leveraged frame, and to test what becomes available.

This distinction is the difference between PM and most therapies. A learner who treats the course as causal-paradigm work will get less out of it.

### 3. Gameworld

The course is, technically, a **gameworld** the learner enters by choice. A gameworld has: explicit rules, defined roles, agreements, consequences, a duration, and a boundary. The Expand the Box gameworld has:

- **Rules:** four working agreements (Safety Framework Section B)
- **Roles:** learner · pairing partner · community manager · CM's supervisor
- **Agreements:** the red-pill commitment, consent practice, partner reachability for High modules
- **Consequences:** specific safety actions when material exceeds scope
- **Duration:** ~30 calendar days, ~10 modules
- **Boundary:** outside the gameworld, ordinary life continues; the gameworld does not colonize it

Naming the course as a gameworld is not casual. It tells the learner that the rules of this space differ from the rules of their default life, and that they are entering an explicit, finite, agreed container — not joining a cult, not becoming a "PM person," and not abandoning what is true elsewhere.

### 4. Archiarchy vs patriarchy

PM is not a self-improvement program inside the dominant culture. It is a thoughtware that points toward a different culture: **archiarchy** — culture organized around bright principles, distributed authority, conscious relating, and creating rather than dominating. **Patriarchy** is the default cultural matrix most learners were raised in: hierarchical, fear-based, control-oriented, and built on numbness.

Archiarchy is not a political identity to adopt. It is a context to test through actions — creating rather than dominating, witnessing rather than controlling, declaring rather than complying, sourcing from bright principles rather than from fear. The course does not require the learner to "become archiarchal." It requires them to notice that many of their default reactions (compete, dominate, comply, withdraw) are patriarchal thoughtware, and to run experiments from a different context. This distinction lands hardest on Day 10 (bright principles, three powers, integration).

### 5. Box layers

The Box is not a single thing. It has layers, and the course addresses different layers in different modules.

- **Surface layer:** behaviors, habits, automatic reactions — the most visible
- **Story layer:** beliefs, rules, conclusions, narratives the learner uses to explain themselves
- **Survival layer:** identity-level commitments formed early, often in response to threat; the layer where the Box says "if I let this go I will die"

A learner who treats every Box signal as a surface-layer habit to tweak will get nowhere. A learner who reaches for the survival layer too early will overwhelm themselves. The course paces this: Day 2 introduces the Box and stays mostly at surface and story; Days 5–6 begin to touch survival-layer material through the emotional body; Day 9 (ego states) gives the learner the tools to work survival material more safely.

### 6. Awareness vs consciousness

**Awareness** is the capacity to notice. *I am breathing. I am anxious. The room is warm.*

**Consciousness** is awareness + the capacity to hold distinctions and choose from them. *I am noticing anxiety, I can distinguish it from fear, and I can choose to ground rather than react.*

PM is a consciousness training, not an awareness training. Mindfulness practices build awareness. PM uses awareness to install distinctions, then uses the distinctions to enable choice. A learner who confuses the two will think they are doing PM when they are doing meditation.

### 7. Being vs Box vs Gremlin

Three different locations the learner can speak, feel, and choose from. They are not synonyms.

- **Being** — what the learner actually is, prior to the Box. Often experienced as still, curious, present. The learner is not always able to locate Being; that is normal.
- **Box** — the survival-and-protection thoughtware. Speaks to keep the learner safe according to its rules. Confuses itself for the learner.
- **Gremlin** — the part of the learner that wants gremlin food (drama, suffering, righteousness, distraction). Distinct from Box; often louder. Worked directly on Days 7 and 9.

A learner who concludes "my Gremlin is bad" or "my Box is me" has missed the distinction. The course is precise: the Box is not the learner, the Gremlin is not the learner, the learner has both and is not either. This distinction matters most when ego states (Day 9) introduce Parent, Child, Adult, Gremlin, and Demon as separate locations — the framework only works if the learner can hold the Box-vs-Being-vs-Gremlin distinction first.

---

## The learning arc (why this order)

The 10-module arc is not arbitrary. It moves from **container → map → embodiment → relationship → integration**, each module installing what the next module assumes.

| Phase | Days | What this phase installs |
|---|---|---|
| **Container & frame** | 1, 2 | Why the learner is doing this work · the chain of new-context → new-results · the Box as the thing that filters everything else · responsibility as creator-stance not victim-stance |
| **Embodiment infrastructure** | 3, 4 | Liquid state · center, ground, bubble · five bodies · feedback loops · what an "experiment" is |
| **Emotional body** | 5, 6 | Feelings vs. emotions · old map and what it hid · the four feelings as archetypal energies · mixed emotions · the emotional healing process |
| **Relational body** | 7, 8 | Low Drama and the gremlin food economy · listening as possibility · speaking as creation · communication map and completion loops |
| **Integration** | 9, 10 | Ego states · problem ownership · learning spiral · map of possibility · bright/shadow principles · three powers · what the learner takes with them |

**Why container before map.** Day 1 doesn't teach a single PM map. It establishes that the learner is the author of what happens in the next 10 modules. Without this stance, every subsequent map becomes information to consume rather than terrain to walk.

**Why embodiment infrastructure before feelings.** A learner cannot work consciously with anger, sadness, fear or joy if they cannot find their center, ground their energy, or notice what their body is doing. Day 3 installs the equipment. Days 5–6 use it.

**Why emotional before relational.** The Low Drama Triangle (Day 7) is, mechanically, a way of avoiding contact with one's own feelings by routing them through somebody else's. A learner who hasn't yet met their own fear, sadness or anger as energies will not be able to detect when they are using a Persecutor or Victim performance to avoid them.

**Why ego states near the end.** Ego states (Parent, Child, Adult, Gremlin, Demon) cut across everything previously taught. They are the **integration tool** — the lens that lets the learner see what the box does in real time and choose differently.

---

## Module shape (the locked Day template)

Every module is a self-contained `Day NN - …` file with the following sections, in this order:

1. **Header block** — Title · Purpose · Intensity tag (Low / Medium / High) · Core PM Concepts · Learning Outcomes
2. **Maps introduced today** — Cross-links to the relevant Map Notes
3. **Module flow** — Suggested order and rough timing for a learner walking through alone
4. **Concept teaching notes** — The distinction set this module installs (written as if a facilitator were explaining it; learners read it as concentrated text)
5. **Embodied practice (solo)** — One physical/energetic exercise the learner does alone
6. **Partner exchange (async)** — A structured voice-message or scheduled-call exchange with the learner's pairing partner
7. **Between-module experiment** — A small, specific rep the learner runs in their actual life before the next module
8. **Reflection prompts** — Journal questions written to surface what the module made available
9. **Safety callouts for this module** — What may come up · what to do if it does · when to pause and call the buddy or step away
10. **Glossary additions** — Any new PM term introduced today, linked to the Glossary

This template is **locked**. Volume-day sub-agents must follow it exactly. Departures are not stylistic improvements — they are violations of the audit trail that makes the course coherent.

---

## Map Note shape (the locked Map Note template)

Each major map gets its own `Map Notes/M## - …` file with:

1. **Map name** and a one-sentence framing
2. **Visual reference** — pointer to the source image path (read-only)
3. **What the map shows** — the territory the map describes
4. **Key distinctions** — bullet list of the 3–7 cuts this map makes
5. **How to explain it verbally** — a script-ready paragraph the facilitator (or the learner, to a partner) can read or paraphrase
6. **Common misunderstandings** — at least three, each paired with the corrective framing
7. **One embodiment practice** — the simplest exercise that lets the learner *feel* the map rather than just understand it

Map Notes are the course's **distinction-density layer**. They are written terse, with no filler. A learner who has read the relevant module plus its Map Notes has enough distinction-density to try the map responsibly, explain it cleanly to their partner, and — importantly — know when *not* to pretend to be a trainer. The Map Notes train the learner to use the map, not to teach it.

---

## How distinctions cascade

Several PM distinctions become teachable only after earlier ones land. The course is engineered around these dependencies:

- *Box vs. you* (Day 2) becomes operational only after *new context* (Day 1). Without a new context, "I have a box" is just self-criticism.
- *Liquid state* (Day 3) becomes operational only after the Box is visible. The whole point of liquid state is the moment the Box loosens — there has to be a Box to loosen.
- *Feeling vs. emotion* (Day 5) becomes operational only after the five bodies (Day 3) — specifically the distinction between the emotional body (where feelings live) and the intellectual body (where thoughts about feelings live).
- *Low Drama* (Day 7) becomes operational only after the new map of feelings (Day 5) — drama is structurally an avoidance of clean feeling.
- *Three Powers* (Day 10) becomes operational only after *radical responsibility* (Day 1) and *bright principles* (Day 10). Without those, "I declare" is grandiosity.

The course resists letting the learner skip ahead — each module assumes the prior one is at least partly installed.

---

## Five-body learning method

Each module engages multiple bodies on purpose. The intellectual body is the easiest to reach online; it is also the body most likely to swallow PM into "interesting ideas I now know about." So every module includes at least one of the following:

- **Emotional body** — name what is felt; let the feeling move; voice-message it to a partner
- **Physical body** — stand, ground, breathe, walk while listening; move during the embodied practice
- **Energetic body** — center, drop a grounding cord, set a bubble, notice the energetic shift when the box loosens
- **Archetypal body** — locate the part of self speaking (Parent / Child / Adult / Gremlin / Demon); name the bright or shadow principle in play

This is the single most important defense against the course becoming a podcast. A learner who only reads and watches has not done the work, no matter how thorough their notes.

---

## Cohort design (async)

The course does not assume a live facilitator and does not assume synchronous group. It assumes:

- **A learner** working through one module per ~3-day cycle (so the full course runs ~30 days, faster or slower as their life allows)
- **A pairing partner** — another learner the course matches them with for the duration; exchanges happen via voice message or scheduled async call
- **A cohort feed** — a single forum or group voice thread where learners post reflections, questions and witness each other's process; lightly moderated

The pairing partner is structurally essential. Several modules (5, 6, 7, 9) include partner check-ins **before** the high-intensity content as well as after. A learner without an active partner should be discouraged from those modules until pairing is in place.

A facilitator (or community manager) is not required to teach the course — the videos and written modules do that — but is required to:
- Triage cohort-feed posts that suggest a learner is in over their head
- Maintain the referral list
- Re-match partners when pairings drop out
- Hold any optional live integration calls (recommended once mid-course, once at end)

See `02 - Async Delivery Framework.md` for the operational detail.

---

## What the course is designed to evoke (and not)

**Designed to evoke:**
- The direct experience that *the learner has a box and is not the box*
- The direct experience that anger, sadness, fear and joy are distinct, useful, archetypal energies — not problems
- The capacity to detect Low Drama in oneself in real time
- The capacity to listen for possibility and speak from it
- The standing-on of radical responsibility as a default stance rather than a heroic effort
- The lived use of the three powers — choosing, asking dangerous questions, declaring

**Not designed to:**
- Treat clinical conditions (depression, PTSD, addiction, psychosis) — these need licensed care
- Replace ongoing therapy or coaching
- Resolve trauma — PM is precise about distinguishing emotional healing process work (which is in scope) from trauma processing (which is not)
- Make the learner happier in any conventional sense — many learners report that PM makes them *more* able to feel what is actually happening, which can be uncomfortable before it is liberating
- Provide a community for life — the cohort is a temporary container; the work continues in the learner's own life

These boundaries are repeated in `03 - Safety and Facilitation Framework.md` and surface again in each module's safety callouts.

---

## How sub-agent drafters should write

This section is for any future contributor (human or AI) drafting additional modules, Map Notes or experiments.

- **Voice.** Direct, distinction-rich, occasionally blunt. Closer to Callahan than to a corporate L&D writer. Use PM's own vocabulary — "box," "thoughtware," "liquid state," "gremlin food," "is-glue," "bright principles." Do not soften these into "limiting beliefs," "growth zones" or "values."
- **Density.** Each paragraph should carry weight. If a paragraph could be cut without the module losing anything, cut it.
- **Verbs.** Prefer concrete verbs (*notice, name, drop, ground, declare, ask, listen, withdraw*) over abstract ones (*explore, engage with, work on, process*).
- **No motivational filler.** The course is for learners who are already in. Do not pep-talk them.
- **Cite where the distinction comes from when useful.** The 19 numbered videos and the Sparks are named in source-citation footnotes where a learner might want to verify a distinction. The course does not pretend to be original — it is a faithful re-presentation of an existing body of work.
- **Safety is always specific.** Generic "take care of yourself" is not safety. Naming the exact next step (e.g. "if you start dissociating, stop the audio, stand up, put one hand on the wall, name three things you can see") is safety.

---

## Versioning and revision

This document is the **course architecture v1**. The locked Day template (Section *Module shape*) and Map Note template (Section *Map Note shape*) cannot be revised mid-course — only between full cohort runs. The teaching content of individual modules and Map Notes can be revised continuously as the course is used.

---

***

# §  02 — Async Delivery Framework

***

# 02 — Async Delivery Framework

This document is the **operational manual** for running Expand the Box as a self-paced asynchronous online course. It is the document a community manager, course operator, or solo cohort steward should read in full before opening a cohort.

The course is designed to work without a live facilitator on every module. It is **not** designed to work without structure. The structure is here.

---

## A. The learner's week

A learner moves through one module per **~3 days** (faster or slower depending on life). The recommended rhythm for a single module:

| Day | Action | Time |
|---|---|---|
| Day 1 | Watch the module video(s) + read the module write-up | 60–90 min |
| Day 1 | Solo embodied practice | 10–20 min |
| Day 1 or 2 | Record partner check-in (voice message) | 5–10 min |
| Day 2–3 | Run the between-module experiment in real life | passive — happens during ordinary day |
| Day 3 | Listen to partner's reply; record reflection back | 10–15 min |
| Day 3 | Write journal reflections; post one line to cohort feed | 15 min |

Total active time per module: **~2 hours on Low-intensity days, ~3–3.5 hours on High-intensity days (5, 6, 7, 9)** — see each day's header for its own estimate; the per-module figures are authoritative, this is the range. The between-module experiment adds zero scheduled time — it is the rep the learner runs *during* their already-scheduled life (a hard conversation, a meeting, dinner with a partner). The async partner-reply latency (up to a 24h SLA) can extend the calendar time of High modules beyond the active hours, especially Day 6.

At ~3 days per module × 10 modules = **~30 days** end to end. Faster cohorts can compress to 20 days; slower cohorts can stretch to 60. The architecture does not care, as long as the rhythm of *content → practice → experiment → reflection* is preserved.

---

## B. Module artifacts (what the learner actually receives)

Each module delivers, in order:

1. **A short orientation video** (5–10 min) — frame for the module, recorded by a PM trainer or course host. Recommends pace, names intensity tag, points to safety callouts.
2. **The relevant concept lecture(s)** from the source library — one or two of the 19 numbered videos, plus any short mini-lectures (e.g., "What Is Your Box," "The Numbness Bar"). Linked, not re-uploaded, where licensing permits; otherwise mirrored to the course platform with attribution.
3. **The written module file** (`Day NN - …`.md) — the script-grade write-up of the module. The single canonical source for the day.
4. **Map Notes** for the maps introduced today.
5. **The partner prompt** — a one-page handout the learner sends to or shares with their pairing partner.
6. **The experiment card** — a single page with the between-module experiment, framed as a small specific rep.
7. **Reflection journal pages** — printable prompts.

All of the above ships as text or PDF the learner can download. Videos are streamed.

---

## C. Pairing partners

### Pairing as one strand of the training matrix

In PM, a **matrix** is a structured field that holds learning. The Expand the Box matrix is woven from several strands: the learner's declared context (the red-pill commitment), the four working agreements, the body practices (center · ground · bubble · golden cube), the Map Notes the learner studies, the cohort boundary, the CM's gatekeeping, and — one strand among these — **the partner pairing**.

The pairing is not the whole matrix. It is the witness strand. What the partner holds: a structured place to speak the learner's actual material out loud, a witness who listens without advising, a buddy whose presence interrupts isolation on the High modules. What the partner does **not** hold: the learner's safety container, the learner's clinical care, the learner's commitment to the work, or the learner's responsibility for their own state.

This is why the partner agreement (`04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section B) is signed before any exchange, why the pairing tracker exists (Doc 04 Section C), and why a learner without a live pairing cannot unlock High modules. The partner strand is not optional — but neither does it carry weight the other strands are meant to carry.

### Why pairing is structural

Pairing is structural, not optional. The course's relational learning (especially Days 5, 6, 7, 8, 9) depends on a learner having one specific other person to:

- Voice-message before high-intensity modules (so they are accompanied, not alone)
- Voice-message after, to be witnessed
- Practice listening, speaking, completion loops and problem ownership with — using their actual material, not role plays

### C.1 Matching rules

- **Match before Day 1.** Learners cannot start Module 1 without an assigned partner. If a learner enrolls late, match them before content access opens.
- **Match on cadence first, content preference second.** Two learners who can both message daily but live in incompatible time zones will struggle less than two perfectly philosophically matched learners who can only meet weekly.
- **Avoid pre-existing close ties.** Spouses, business partners, very close friends bring entanglement that compromises the practice. If pre-existing ties are unavoidable in a small cohort, name the dynamic explicitly and add a third "witness partner."
- **Re-match by Day 4 if it isn't working.** If the partnership has not produced one real exchange by Day 4, the community manager re-matches. Silent partnerships are worse than swapped ones.

### C.2 Voice-message exchanges (the default mode)

Voice messages are preferred to text. They carry tone, breath, and the texture of the learner's emotional body — text strips this. Recommended platforms: Telegram, WhatsApp, Voxer, or Signal. The course does not impose one, **but the platform must meet the privacy minimums in `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section H** — private 1:1 thread, no automatic AI transcription, no public forwarding, deletion option, and (preferably) end-to-end encryption. Public Discord servers, group chats, and platforms that auto-summarize voice notes do not qualify.

**Default exchange shape per module:**
- Learner A records 3–8 min responding to the module's partner prompt
- Learner B listens within 24 hours, then records 3–8 min back: *what I heard · what I noticed in myself · one question I'm leaving with you*
- Optionally: a second round if either partner wants it

**What partners do NOT do:**
- Advise
- Fix
- Diagnose
- "Hold space" in a generic way
- Pretend to feel something they do not feel

What they do is **listen, witness, and reflect back what they actually heard**. The course teaches this on Day 8 (4 Listenings + Speakings). Until then, learners have an explicit "we're learning this" frame for any clumsy exchange.

### C.3 Scheduled async calls (alternative)

For partners who prefer real-time voice over recorded voice messages, a 30-minute scheduled call substitutes for the exchange. Same structure: each partner gets ~10 min uninterrupted, with the other listening.

---

## D. The cohort feed

A single shared space — forum thread, Slack/Discord channel, group voice thread, or shared doc — where learners post brief reflections after each module.

**What learners post:**
- One line of what landed
- One line of what is sticking sideways
- (Optional) a question for the group
- (Optional) a witness offer: "if anyone needs a third party to listen to something this week, I have 20 min Thursday"

**What learners do NOT post:**
- Long therapeutic confessionals (the partner exchange is the place for that)
- Other people's stories
- Advice to peers (community manager redirects)

**Cohort feed moderation:**
- Community manager reads every post within 48 hours
- Every post is classified into one of three flags using the green/yellow/red **triage rubric** in `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section F. Yellow = DM within 24 hours. Red = immediate response (not within 24 hours), with crisis line numbers in the first message.
- Keeps the feed *narrow* — broad debate about PM theory belongs in a different forum

---

## E. Optional live integration calls

The course is async-first. Two **optional live calls** are recommended for any cohort:

1. **Mid-course integration call** — **after Day 6 (not after Day 5).** ~75 min. Facilitator-led. Placed here on purpose: Days 5, 6 and 7 are three High-intensity modules in a row, and Day 6 (the EHP) is the single heaviest. The call lands *after the learner is through the worst of the cliff and before Day 7*, so it functions as integration and a breath, not a warm-up. Format: short check-in round, one or two volunteer "live demos" of the new map of feelings / a recent EHP-map practice on a real situation, Q&A.
2. **End-of-course integration call** — after Day 10. ~90 min. Facilitator-led. Format: declarations round (each learner declares one thing they are taking forward), gratitude round to partners, what's-next pointers (further training, communities, books).

### The integration pause (built into the cadence, not optional)

**Insert a deliberate rest beat between Day 6 and Day 7.** This is the only place in the course where three High modules stack. After Day 6's EHP practice the learner is often tender for hours; opening Day 7 (Low Drama, the Gremlin) on top of that is how cohorts burn out or silently drop. The CM holds the cadence here: at least **one full low-demand day** between Day 6 and Day 7 — no new content, just ground, sleep, journal, and a partner check-in. Day 7's header repeats this. Learners on the compressed cadence (Doc Section I) still take this pause; it is not a module they can skip past.

**Recording rules.** Personal check-ins, demos, and shares are **never recorded.** Recording is permitted only for the teaching/Q&A segments and only if every participant in the call gives explicit consent at the start of that specific call. Consent given for one call does not carry forward. For absent learners, the facilitator provides a written summary of the teaching content (not the shares). See `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section H.

Live calls are *integration* — they don't introduce new content. A learner who skips them does not miss material.

---

## F. The community manager role

A community manager (CM) — often the cohort facilitator, but not necessarily a PM trainer — is required to operate a cohort safely. The CM is not the teacher; the modules are. The CM is the **container caretaker**.

### CM responsibilities

- **Pre-cohort:** matches partners; sends welcome packet; confirms each learner has the referral list (Section H) and knows how to reach the CM
- **Per-module:** monitors cohort feed; checks partner exchanges are happening (not their content — just that they exist); replies to direct messages within 24 hours
- **High-intensity weeks (Days 5–7):** lightweight check-in DM to every learner ("how's it landing? anything to flag?"); does not require a reply
- **Closure:** reminds learners how to access materials post-cohort; offers continued partner-pairing if both want it
- **Always:** holds the referral list; refers any learner who is over their head to professional support; does not provide therapy or coaching themselves

### CM skill floor

The CM is not necessarily a certified PM trainer or the teaching trainer for the cohort. But the role is non-trivial — see `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section J for the binding qualification bar: minimum completed Expand the Box plus one further PM training, current mental health first aid certification, a named clinical supervisor for case consultation, a written CM agreement with the operator, and professional liability insurance appropriate for the jurisdiction.

The skill floor (necessary but not sufficient) is the ability to:
- Hold confidentiality cleanly
- Distinguish emotional intensity (in scope) from crisis (out of scope)
- Refer without flinching
- Not collapse into rescuer mode when learners are uncomfortable
- Apply the triage rubric and the crisis escalation flow in Doc 04 Sections F and G without freezing

The CM's job is to keep the container intact. It is not to ensure no one feels uncomfortable. PM work involves discomfort. The container's job is to make discomfort survivable, not absent.

---

## G. Platform requirements

The course does not impose a platform. It needs:

- **Video hosting** (any platform that supports streaming and download for the concept videos)
- **Document hosting** (the `.md` files and PDFs of module write-ups, Map Notes, experiment cards, journal prompts)
- **Voice-message platform** (partner choice)
- **Cohort feed** (a forum, Slack/Discord, group thread)
- **A way for the CM to message learners 1:1**

Total: any combination of (Teachable / Podia / Kajabi / Notion / Circle) + (Telegram / WhatsApp / Voxer) + (Slack / Discord) works.

---

## H. The referral list

Every learner receives, at enrollment, a **per-learner referral packet** generated from the country, state/province, and language they declared at intake (see `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section A.1). The packet contains:

1. **One crisis line for the learner's country** — listed first, not buried
2. **Licensed mental health professionals** in the learner's region — directory link + any known PM-friendly clinicians
3. **PM-aware coaches** in the learner's language, with rates
4. **Local domestic violence and legal resources** if the coercive-environment screen returned yes
5. **A short not-therapy disclaimer**

The packet is generated and acknowledged **before** content access opens. The CM verifies. A generic facility-template version lives at `Facilitator Resources/Referral List.md`; the per-learner packet is the operational artifact.

---

## I. Cadence variants

| Variant | Pace | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| **Default** | ~3 days per module, ~30 days total | Best for most learners |
| **Compressed** | ~2 days per module, ~20 days total | Only for learners with bandwidth; risks shallow integration |
| **Stretched** | 4–6 days per module, 40–60 days total | Good for learners with demanding lives; works as long as the rhythm holds |
| **Pulsed** | Modules 1–2 in week 1, break 1 week, modules 3–4 in week 3, etc. | Good if life requires it; community manager makes sure partner pairings are still alive at re-entry |

Pace decisions are the learner's. The CM informs the partner so cadences match.

---

## J. What this framework deliberately leaves out

- **Gamification, badges, streaks, completion certificates.** They feed Gremlin's appetite for approval, comparison, and completion points. PM does not reward compliance.
- **Discussion forums for "questions about PM."** They become content consumption. The course's intellectual content is fixed; debate it elsewhere.
- **Replay-able quizzes.** PM is verified in lived experience, not multiple choice.
- **An app.** A platform is enough.

The framework is deliberately spare. The course's force is in the modules and the partner pairings, not in the infrastructure around them.

---

<sub>🄯 **World Copyleft 2026** · *Expand the Box (Digital)* · licensed **[CC BY-SA 4.0](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0/)** · re-presents Possibility Management thoughtware originated by Clinton Callahan & the Possibility Management community · please share, share-alike · Powered by Possibility Management ([possibilitymanagement.org](https://possibilitymanagement.org)) · full terms: `LICENSE.md` in the course root</sub>

***

# §  03 — Safety and Facilitation Framework

***

# 03 — Safety and Facilitation Framework

> This document is the operational safety baseline for Expand the Box delivered async online.
> A community manager (CM) should read it cover-to-cover before opening a cohort.
> A learner should read sections **B**, **C**, **D**, **F** and **I** before starting Day 1.

---

## A. What this course is not

**Expand the Box is not:**
- Therapy
- Counseling
- Trauma treatment
- Medical or psychiatric care
- A substitute for any of the above

It is an educational course in the thoughtware of Possibility Management. It will bring into view: Box survival strategies the learner has been identified with, feelings that have been unfelt, numbness in places that used to be alive, Low Drama payoffs the learner has been collecting, old decisions made under threat that are still running. That is by design. Discomfort is part of the work. Discomfort that overwhelms the learner is **not** part of the work and is the cue to pause and reach for professional support.

A learner who is currently:
- In acute mental health crisis
- Newly bereaved (within the last 60 days, as a default — case by case)
- In the active middle of a major life rupture (separation, job loss, eviction, recent diagnosis)
- Unable to center, ground, drop a bubble, return to Adult, or feel 10% of a feeling without becoming it
- Without a current therapist or coach for material that is already in process

…should **wait** to take this course, take it slowly with active professional support alongside, or take it later. The CM applies the **full intake screening protocol** in `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section A — five specific screens (suicidality, trauma & dissociation, addiction, coercive environment, mania/psychosis) with explicit thresholds and actions. The screening is the gate, not a recommendation.

---

## B. The four working agreements

A learner who begins Day 1 is agreeing to four things. They are repeated at the start of every module.

1. **Choice is always available.** The learner can pause, skip a practice, slow down, take a longer break between modules, or stop entirely. Nothing in the course is mandatory. No PM teacher anywhere requires a learner to "push through" anything. If the learner's body says no, the answer is no.
2. **Consent is ongoing.** The course asks the learner's consent at the start of each high-intensity practice. Consent given at enrollment does not carry forward into every exercise. The learner can withdraw consent for any single practice and continue with the course.
3. **The learner is responsible for their own state.** The course teaches the practices: center, ground, drop a bubble, feel, choose, ask, declare. The learner practices using them. A facilitator is not present in real time. If the learner cannot access the practices in a given moment, they pause and reach for support — buddy, CM, or the referral list.
4. **The buddy/partner is alive.** Before starting Days 5, 6, 7 and 9, the learner confirms their pairing partner is reachable. If not, the module waits until pairing is in place. This is not a suggestion. It is a structural requirement.

---

## C. Intensity tags

Every module is tagged Low / Medium / High intensity. The tag is in the header block and influences pacing and partner check-in requirements.

| Tag | Days | Meaning |
|---|---|---|
| **Low** | 1, 3, 4, 10 | Material is largely cognitive and embodied-light. May still surface feeling but is unlikely to put the learner in unfamiliar territory. No required partner check-in before the module. **Note: Day 3 is Low *emotional* intensity but is structurally load-bearing — it installs the center/ground/bubble/cube equipment every High module depends on. Do not skim it.** |
| **Medium** | 2, 8 | Day 2: disidentification + Box inventory + survival-layer preview (the highest-charge front-half module). Day 8: direct relational practice using the learner's actual material — for many, as intense as feelings work. **Partner check-in recommended before starting; debrief after.** |
| **High** | 5, 6, 7, 9 | Material directly engages the emotional body, drama patterns, ego states, or the gremlin. May surface material the learner has not seen before. **Required partner check-in before starting; required partner debrief after. High modules are gated by the unlock checklist in `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section D.** |

There is **no skip-after-24-hours override** for High-module partner check-in. The earlier framework permitted this; it is retracted. If a learner cannot meet the unlock checklist, they wait. The course will still be there in a week.

---

## D. The universal grounding script

Available at the top of every module file as a callout box. Reproduced here:

> **Grounding (60 seconds).**
> 1. Stop whatever you were doing in the module. Close the video or the document.
> 2. Stand up. Both feet on the floor. Knees soft.
> 3. Breathe out longer than you breathe in, three times. Audible exhale is fine.
> 4. Name three things you can see in the room.
> 5. Name one thing you can hear.
> 6. Place one hand on your sternum, the other on your belly. Notice that your body is here.
> 7. When you have come back, decide: continue, pause for 10 minutes, or stop the module for today.

This script is the default action whenever a learner notices any of the following:
- Feeling far away from themselves
- Inability to follow the words on the page or in the video
- Heart racing without clear cause
- The sense that they are watching themselves from outside
- Crying that does not feel like a clean feeling but feels stuck
- Strong urge to flee, attack, or shut down

These are signals to ground first, then decide. They are not signals that something is wrong with the learner. They are signals that the nervous system needs a beat.

---

## E. When to pause the module

The course teaches a clean distinction:

- **Discomfort that is moving** → keep going gently. This is the work.
- **Discomfort that is stuck or escalating** → ground (Section D), then pause for at least 10 minutes, then re-decide.
- **Discomfort that is unmistakably crisis** → stop, contact the buddy, and if needed the referral list (Section H).

The learner does not have to perfectly classify their state. The default action when uncertain is to ground and pause. The course losing 10 minutes to caution is fine. The learner pushing through a state that needed a pause is not.

---

## F. When to call the buddy

The partner pairing is not just for the structured exchanges. It is also a real-time resource. A learner should send the buddy a voice message — short, no production — in any of the following situations:

- They notice they have been in a stuck feeling for more than 24 hours
- They notice they have been numbing (substances, screens, work, food) more than usual since the module
- They had a strong reaction during the module and want to be witnessed
- They are about to do something significant in their life that the module surfaced (have a difficult conversation, leave a job, end a relationship) — partner is not advisor; partner is witness
- They notice they are stalling on the next module and want to talk about why

Buddies do not advise. Buddies witness, reflect, and ask the buddy questions taught in Days 8 and 9. If the buddy is over their head, **the buddy contacts the CM**, not the original learner's professional support. The CM decides whether to escalate.

### Buddy immediate-danger protocol

> **If your partner tells you they may harm themselves or someone else, ask: "Are you in immediate danger right now?"**
>
> If **yes** — contact local emergency services or your country's crisis line AND the CM **immediately.** Do not wait for course protocol. Do not wait for the CM's 24-hour SLA. Stay with your partner in the message thread until they have connected with crisis services.
>
> If **no** — voice-message the CM the same day. The CM will reach out to your partner directly.

This rule is part of the partner agreement every partner signs before pairing (see `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section B). A partner who has not signed it is not eligible for the buddy role.

---

## G. When to call the CM

The CM is reachable by direct message with a guaranteed reply within 24 hours **for routine messages.** For active crisis (red flag in the triage rubric — Doc 04 Section F), the standard is **immediate on detection, with first response within 15 minutes** of the CM (or named backup) seeing the message, crisis line numbers in that first reply. The CM ensures a named backup with accepted role + platform access + crisis protocol covers any window when the CM is unreachable.

A learner reaches the CM when:

- They want to pause the cohort for personal reasons
- Their partner is unresponsive or the pairing is not working
- Something happened in their life since enrollment that affects whether they should continue
- They are concerned about another learner in the cohort
- They want a referral

The CM does **not** provide coaching or therapy. The CM helps the learner make a structural decision and points to resources.

---

## H. The referral pathway

The referral list (`Facilitator Resources/Referral List.md`) is included in the welcome packet. It contains, per region:

1. PM-aware coaches (from the PM Trainer Path graduate directory)
2. Licensed mental health professionals (general directories the learner can search; PM-friendly clinicians where known)
3. Crisis lines and emergency contacts

The template list lives in `Facilitator Resources/Referral List.md`. The operational artifact is the **per-learner referral packet** generated from intake (see `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section E) and confirmed before content access opens.

**The CM refers to the list when:**
- A learner expresses suicidal ideation, intent or plan → crisis line first, then licensed clinician
- A learner is processing material clearly beyond the course's scope (active trauma, abuse history, addiction) → licensed clinician
- A learner wants 1:1 PM-aware support beyond the partner pairing → PM-aware coach
- A learner is well and wants to deepen → PM Trainer Path or local PM community

**Referral language template (CM, when needed):**
> What I'm hearing is bigger than what the course is built to hold. That doesn't mean you're doing the work wrong — it means the work you're doing right now needs someone qualified to be with you in it. Here are three options: [coach / clinician / line]. The course will be here when you come back. Do you want me to put the cohort on pause for you?

---

## I. Consent practice (start of every High-intensity module)

Each High-intensity module opens with a short consent prompt. The learner reads it and decides. Verbatim:

> **Consent check.**
> This module engages [feelings / drama patterns / ego states / etc.] directly. Material that has been managed by avoidance may surface. You are choosing to do this.
>
> Before continuing, confirm to yourself:
> - My partner is reachable today and tomorrow.
> - I have at least 90 uninterrupted minutes ahead of me.
> - I am not in acute crisis or under the influence right now.
> - I know how to ground (see top of file).
> - I know how to reach the CM if I need to.
>
> If any of the above is not true, pause this module and come back when it is.
> If all of the above is true and you choose to continue, take a slow breath and begin.

This is not bureaucratic. It is the consent moment that distinguishes a chosen practice from a thing happening to the learner.

---

## J. Special-population notes

- **Survivors of trauma.** PM is precise that *emotional healing process work* (in scope) is distinct from *trauma processing* (not in scope). Survivors should be in concurrent care with a trauma-qualified clinician and check with that clinician about whether to take the course now or later. The CM does not screen these clinically.
- **Learners on psychiatric medication.** PM does not contraindicate medication. The course does not advise changing medication. Any medication question goes to the prescribing physician.
- **Neurodivergent learners.** The course's pacing assumes the learner can self-regulate length-of-engagement and break frequency. Neurodivergent learners may need the stretched cadence (Section I of the Async Delivery Framework). The CM should ask, not assume.
- **Learners in current grief.** Recent loss + this course can be productive or destabilizing depending on the loss, the time elapsed, and the learner's support system. Default: encourage waiting at least 60 days post-loss and ensuring a current therapist or grief-aware coach is alongside.

---

## K. CM safety practices (for the CM, not the learner)

- **Read every cohort-feed post within 48 hours.** No exceptions.
- **Log direct-message exchanges** (date, learner, summary, action taken). Brief is fine. The log protects the learner and the CM.
- **Keep the referral list current.** Quarterly check that listed clinicians and coaches are still practicing and accepting clients.
- **Refer without flinching.** A CM who delays referral because they want to "help first" is contributing to harm.
- **Hold confidentiality.** Cohort-feed posts are not shared outside the cohort. Direct-message exchanges are not shared with the learner's partner or with other learners. The only exceptions: imminent risk of harm, legal compulsion, or the learner's own explicit consent.
- **Have a CM-side check-in.** The CM should themselves have a supervisor, peer, or coach to debrief with. Holding a cohort is real work.

---

## L. Incident response (if something goes wrong)

If a learner experiences a serious adverse event during or attributable to the course (psychiatric crisis, hospitalization, significant rupture):

1. **CM contacts the learner** — immediately if active crisis (red flag); within 24 hours otherwise. Plain language. Asks what happened, what they need, whether they are safe right now.
2. **CM offers** pause, refund, referral, or continued cohort access — the learner chooses.
3. **CM documents** the incident factually and confidentially.
4. **CM debriefs** with their own supervisor or peer.
5. **CM reviews** the course content the learner had been engaging with. If a pattern emerges across multiple learners with the same module, the module is revised before the next cohort.

This is not a defensive posture. It is the minimum honest response to material that engages people's inner lives.

---

## M. Three things this document does not pretend

1. **It does not pretend the course is safe in all cases.** It is safe for most adults who self-select into a thoughtware course and engage with reasonable care. It is not appropriate for everyone. The screening, the pacing controls and the referral pathway exist because of this.
2. **It does not pretend the CM is a therapist.** A CM holding a cohort with this framework is doing real and skilled work, but it is the work of a community caretaker, not a clinician.
3. **It does not pretend that doing nothing is also safe.** Many of the learners drawn to this course are already in pain — pain that the absence of PM-grade thoughtware was not preventing. The decision to take the course (or to recommend it) is always weighed against the alternative of continuing without it.

---
