# §  M26 - Rapid Learning

***

# M26 — Rapid Learning

*The fast inner loop by which a person upgrades thoughtware in ordinary life — Go! → Beep! → Shift! → Go! — and the one swamp that kills it.*

![Map of Rapid Learning — Possibility Management map](../Maps/M26.png)

**What it is.** The map is a loop, not a line: three stations on a wheel that keeps turning. **GO!** — you act, you try the thing. **BEEP!** — something did not work as planned. **SHIFT!** — you change one specific variable and run again, the arrow back to GO! being the do-over that is the whole point. The BEEP! box carries the correction — *This is NOT a failure* — because a Beep! is design data, not a verdict. Both Go! and Beep! are feedback. The loop only dies when Beep! collapses into "I am bad" and the actor slides off the wheel into the **Feedback Swamp**.

**At a glance.** Loop → Go! → Beep! → Shift! → Go! (the last arrow is the do-over) · Go! = worked · Beep! = didn't work as planned — both are feedback · A Beep! is design data, not a verdict on your worth · A Shift! is one specific variable, not your whole identity · Feedback Swamp → "oh no / I can't do anything right / they're attacking me" — the wheel jams · Exit → "Thank you for the feedback," log it in the Beep! Book, name the Shift!, Go! again.

---

>
> - **Full teaching →** [Day 4 — Feedback, Coaching, Rapid Learning, Experiments](../Days/Day%2004%20-%20Feedback%2C%20Coaching%2C%20Rapid%20Learning%2C%20Experiments.md)

# §  M27 - Your Gremlin

***

# M27 — Your Gremlin

*The King or Queen of your Underworld — the part of you that wants drama, suffering and righteousness as food, and runs your life from below your awareness until you meet it on purpose.*

![Your Gremlin — Possibility Management map](../Maps/M27.png)

**What it is.** A hand-drawn portrait, not a diagram — the Gremlin drawn as a resident so you stop treating it as an abstraction. It is the part of you that wants **gremlin food**: drama, suffering, righteousness, being right, being a victim, being special, distraction. Sovereign below your awareness — the King or Queen of your Underworld — and the map states the cost plainly: until you meet it consciously, *it owns your life.* It is distinct from Being and from the Box (the Box wants safety; the Gremlin wants food), it speaks in a voice that feels true, and it eats *"I'm the worst"* and *"I'm the best"* with equal appetite.

**At a glance.** Wants food, not safety (the cut from the Box) · Distinct from Being and Box — *you have it, you are not it* · Speaks *sotto voce* in a voice that passes for insight · On a low-drama feast right now (M13): the sigh, the eye-roll, the rehearsed righteousness · Eats both directions — grandiosity and self-disgust are the same meal · Not the enemy, cannot be killed — meet it, know it, befriend it, put it to use. **Scope:** meeting and naming your Gremlin is in scope here; deep Gremlin process work (Gremlin Transformation) is a separate container held by a PM trainer / the GT training — same discipline as the Demon scope note in M17. Do not attempt to "transform" it solo.

---

# §  M28 - Gameworld

***

# M28 — Gameworld

*A gameworld is a field of human commitment with a context, a purpose, and rules of engagement — and naming the one you are inside is what turns unconscious drift into chosen action.*

![Gameworld — Possibility Management map](../Maps/M28.png)

**What it is.** A gameworld is a field of human **commitment** — every word load-bearing. *Field*: it has an inside and an outside. *Human*: people bring it into being and sustain it. *Commitment*: it is held together by what the people inside have agreed to keep doing, not by walls. "Game" does not mean trivial — it means bounded, ruled, and chosen. A marriage, a company, this course are all gameworlds. Most of patriarchal life runs as *unconscious* gameworlds whose rules nobody named; consciousness is the move of seeing the one you are in, reading its real rules, and choosing to keep, renegotiate, or leave.

**At a glance.** A field of commitment, not "a game" — *game* names the structure, the stakes are fully real · Three load-bearing parts → Context (practical relationship with responsibility) · Purpose (agreed origination + intention + commitment to create) · Rules of Engagement (the agreements of operation) · You ENTER by choice (Day 1's red-pill) and LEAVE consciously (Day 10) · Naming makes the rules explicit — and negotiable · Bounded by a duration, so naming it is safe not cultish · Most of your life already runs as gameworlds; the question is whether you can see them.

---

>
> - **Full teaching →** [Day 1 — Orientation, New Context, Radical Responsibility](../Days/Day%2001%20-%20Orientation%2C%20New%20Context%2C%20Radical%20Responsibility.md)

# §  M29 - Map of Reactivities

***

# M29 — Map of Reactivities

*Six different kinds of automatic reaction — Buttons, Voices, Activated Traumas, Hooks, Triggers, Imbalances — that all feel the same from inside but each route to a different tool, so the first move is always to name which one fired.*

![Map of Reactivities — Possibility Management map](../Maps/M29.png)

**What it is.** A reactivity is when something external sets off an automatic internal reaction that is *not* a present-time conscious choice — you are already reacting before you decided to. The load-bearing claim: not all reactivity is the same kind, and each kind has a different antidote. From the inside they all feel identical — a jolt, a charge, a sudden *no* — so the untrained move is to reach for one favorite tool every time. The map says stop and ask *which of the six is this?*, because a Button needs Box work, an Activated Trauma the EHP, and an Imbalance just food, rest, or grounding. Misdiagnosing the kind applies the wrong tool, and the wrong tool does nothing.

**At a glance.** Buttons → Box rules firing → Expand the Box (M04) · Voices → swallowed authority figures → shoot the voices · Activated Traumas → the past flooding the present → EHP (M12) for the in-scope stored emotion; actual trauma goes to a clinician, not the EHP · Hooks → gremlin seductions into low drama → decline the gremlin food · Triggers → specific draining sentences / "vampires" → close the cake · Imbalances → a tired/hungry/leaking 5-body (M06), not psychological → bring the body to balance. **Diagnostic move:** name the kind first; the name tells you the route.

---

> **This is a map card.** The full teaching and practice now live in two places:
>
> - **Full teaching →** [Day 7 — Low Drama, Gremlin Food, Shifting to the Responsible Game](../Days/Day%2007%20-%20Low%20Drama%2C%20Gremlin%20Food%2C%20Shifting%20to%20Responsible%20Game.md)
> - **Interactive tool →** [Map Atlas · M29 Map of Reactivities](../Map%20Atlas/M29%20-%20Map%20of%20Reactivities.html)

# §  Async Partner Pairing Playbook

***

# Async Partner Pairing Playbook

| | |
|---|---|
| **For** | Community Manager (CM) running an async Expand the Box cohort |
| **When** | Open this file before matching begins and keep it open through cohort close |
| **Replaces** | The in-person "Breakout Room Designs" document |
| **Reads alongside** | `02 - Async Delivery Framework.md` Section C · `03 - Safety and Facilitation Framework.md` Sections B, F · `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Sections A, B, C, D, I |

The pairing IS the matrix — the energetic infrastructure that lets the learner stay in their body while their thoughtware is upgrading. Without a working pairing, the modules become information. With one, transformation. Treat the matrix as load-bearing.

Doc 04 holds the protocols (partner agreement, tracker fields, unlock checklist, mismatch logic). This playbook holds the language — verbatim CM voice messages, per-module exchange shapes, and the decision trees that keep the matrix intact.

---

## 1. Pre-cohort — matching learners

Matching happens before content access opens. A learner cannot start Module 1 without an assigned partner. Late enrollees: match first, open content second.

**Inputs** (from Doc 04 Section A.1): time zone and weekly availability windows · primary language · cadence declaration (Default / Compressed / Stretched / Pulsed) · country and state/province.

**Rules, in priority order.**

1. **Cadence first.** Same cadence variant only. Never match a Compressed learner with a Stretched learner — you will be re-matching by Day 4.
2. **Time zone within 6 hours.** A 24h SLA dies fast when one partner is asleep two-thirds of the window. If two cadence-matched learners are >6h apart, prefer a less-cadence-matched pair inside 6h.
3. **Shared primary language.** Voice messages carry tone; tone does not translate. Same language only.
4. **No pre-existing close ties.** Spouses, business partners, very close friends bring entanglement that compromises the practice. If unavoidable in a small cohort, name the dynamic explicitly and add a witness partner from the start (Section 6).
5. **Algorithmic fallback.** Two equally-good matches: pair the earlier-enrolled learner with the closer-availability partner. The later learner gets second-best. Latecomers do not bump earlier learners.

**Do not match on** age, gender, profession, content interest, "vibe." None of these predict whether the pairing will produce a real exchange by Day 4. Cadence does.

**Solo learners.** Odd-numbered cohort: the CM is the partner for the leftover learner for the first week only, then re-match when the next cohort starts or a witness partner volunteers (Section 6). The CM as partner is a stopgap — it compromises triage neutrality.

---

## 2. The partner-pairing welcome email

CM sends within 24h of matching, BCC'd to both partners. Voice-message-ready; the CM can also record and send a voice version.

```
Subject: Your Expand the Box partner — [Partner B's first name]

Hi [A] and [B],

You two are paired for this cohort. You are not each other's
therapist, coach, or fixer. You are each other's witness. The course
teaches witnessing step by step; for now — listen, reflect what you
heard, ask one honest question. That is the whole job.

BEFORE YOU EXCHANGE ANYTHING, both of you sign the partner agreement
below. Reply-all "signed" to confirm. A learner who has not signed
is not eligible for pairing, and pairing is required to unlock the
course.

The partner agreement (verbatim):

  1. I will respond to my partner's voice message within 24 hours,
     even if briefly.
  2. I will not advise, fix, or diagnose. I will witness.
  3. I will hold what my partner shares in confidence.
  4. If my partner tells me they may harm themselves or someone else,
     I will ask: "Are you in immediate danger right now?" If yes,
     I will contact local emergency or crisis services AND the CM
     immediately. I will not wait for course protocol.
  5. If I become unable to be in the partnership, I will tell the CM
     within 48 hours so a re-match happens.
  6. I will not use what my partner shares in any other context.
  7. I will not enter a sexual, financial, or professional
     relationship with my partner during the course.

PLATFORM. Pick a private 1:1 voice-message tool. Acceptable:
Telegram, WhatsApp (E2EE on), Voxer, Signal. Not acceptable: Discord
servers, group chats, anything that auto-transcribes with AI.
Confirm to me which you chose.

FIRST EXCHANGE — the Day 1 partner prompt (attached as PDF).
Record 3-8 minutes: who you are · what is alive in you about being
here · what you specifically came for. Listen to your partner's
message all the way through, then reply 3-8 minutes: what you heard ·
what you noticed in yourself while listening · one open question.
Speak from your body. Stumbles stay in. Do not edit.

DEADLINES.
  - Within 24 hours: agreement signed.
  - Within 48 hours: platform chosen.
  - Within 72 hours: first voice message sent.
  - If your partner stops responding for >24 hours or the pairing
    feels unworkable — tell me, not them. Silent unworkable pairings
    are worse than swapped ones.

I do not read your exchanges. I track only that they happened. The
only confidentiality exception is agreement item 4.

— [CM name]
```

Attachments: partner agreement PDF, the Day 1 partner prompt PDF, and the per-learner referral packet re-attached as a reminder.

---

## 3. Per-module partner-exchange template

The exchange shape stays the same across all 10 modules. The prompt content lives in each `Day NN - …` file under "Partner exchange (async)." The CM does not author per-module prompts — points to them, confirms the shape is held.

### Generic shape (every module)

```
A records 3-8 min (5-10 min for High modules):
  - Responds to the module's three-point partner prompt
  - Speaks from the body, not from a script; stumbles stay in
  - Voice message only (or scheduled call — Doc 02 Section C.3)

B listens within 24h, all the way through once, then records 3-7 min:
  1. What I heard you say — the part that landed
  2. What I noticed in myself while listening — feeling, body 
     sensation, thought
  3. One open question I'm leaving with you — lands in the body

NO advice, NO fixing, NO "have you tried," NO "I had a similar 
experience." Witnessing only. Optional second round if either wants.
```

### Three worked examples

**Day 1 (Low) — Orientation, New Context, Radical Responsibility.** Prompt: who you are · what is alive in you about being in this course · what you specifically came for. The first exchange is almost always awkward. The welcome email pre-warns ("awkwardness is not danger; first reps are clumsy") so neither partner reads the awkwardness as a bad sign.

**Day 5 (High) — Feelings vs Emotions, Old Map of Feelings, Numbness Bar.** Prompt: one specific rule from your Old Map of Feelings (e.g., *"in my family, anger meant my father had been drinking, so I learned: if you feel angry, leave the room"*) · what surfaced in the Low-Intensity Feelings practice (which feelings registered with which objects, whether you hit the Numbness Bar) · one feeling alive in you right now in the form *"Right now I feel some [feeling], the sensation is [location and quality], what I think it is about is [one sentence]."* Reply: what you heard · what feeling surfaced in you while listening, named/located/intensity-noted — *"I felt some sadness in my throat, low intensity, maybe 10%"* · one open question. If a partner names an emotion (feeling about something years ago, story attached, >5 minutes), the listener gently names it as out-of-scope and points to the CM. Day 6 is for emotional healing process; Day 5 is for registering.

**Day 8 (Medium) — Listening, Speaking, Communication, Completion Loops.** The exchange IS the module. Partners schedule 45 min synchronous if possible. Each speaks 5 min about something genuinely alive; the other holds Possibility Listening (no nodding, no smiling, no questions). At the 5-min mark the listener replies with exactly three statements: *"What I heard you say was…" · "What I noticed in myself was…" · "The question I am leaving with you is…"* Then they reverse. Both end with the explicit completion loop: *"Are we complete on this exchange?" — "Yes."* The CM sends a 24-hour-advance reminder DM: *"Day 8 is the relational practice module. The exchange IS the module. Find 45 min with your partner this week."*

---

## 4. The 24-hour SLA enforcement protocol

The pairing tracker (Doc 04 Section C) flags missed SLAs mechanically. The trigger rules do the remembering for the CM.

**Trigger 1 — one missed SLA in a single module.** No action. Life happens; the pairing self-corrects most of the time.

**Trigger 2 — missed SLA twice in one module.** CM voice-messages BOTH partners (not just the silent one). Same message to both:

```
Hi [name] — cadence dropped on Module [N] with [partner]. Not 
asking what's in the exchange — I don't read those. Checking the 
structure: is the pairing still working?

Three options:
  1. Fine, life was just full — we'll catch up. Reply "fine."
  2. Something's off but workable — tell me, we'll talk.
  3. Not working — I'll re-match. No story needed.

Reply by [date, ~48h]. No reply = option 3.
```

**Trigger 3 — missed SLA in two consecutive modules.** CM offers a re-match. Same message to both:

```
Hi [name] — cadence has dropped two modules in a row with [partner]. 
That's the pattern where I step in.

I'm re-matching unless you tell me by [date, 48h] that you have a 
specific plan to get back on rhythm. No judgment. The modules ahead 
([list 2 upcoming]) lean on the matrix being live.

Re-match, or specific plan?
```

**Trigger 4 — one partner has not initiated in 6 days.** CM unilaterally offers the silent partner's responsive partner a re-match:

```
Hi [name] — [partner] hasn't initiated in 6 days. That leaves you 
without a working witness, and you have [Module N: a High] coming. 
I'm re-matching you. The other learner stays in the cohort; the 
silence is between them and me.

New partner within 48h. Same 7-line agreement and platform setup 
apply. If you'd rather wait a few more days for [original partner], 
tell me. Default is re-match.
```

---

## 5. The re-match protocol

Re-matching is not failure. It is the matrix self-correcting. The CM frames it that way every time.

**When to re-match.**
- Trigger 2 (Section 4), if either partner chose option 3
- Trigger 3, if no specific plan
- Trigger 4, default
- Either partner requests it, with or without a reason
- A Yellow or Red flag in either partner's DMs names the pairing as part of the problem
- A pre-existing close-tie pairing turns out to be too entangled (Section 1, rule 4)

**Who to re-match the now-single learner to**, in order of preference: another single learner from a re-match elsewhere in the cohort · a learner whose original partner withdrew · a waitlisted learner from the same cohort · a witness partner from the bench (Section 6) for one module until a permanent re-match arrives.

**Language to the re-paired learners.** Use the welcome email template (Section 2), replacing the opener with:

```
Hi [A] and [B],

Re-pairing — you two are now paired for the rest of this cohort. 
Re-matching is normal; about one in four cohorts has one. It is 
not a failure of either of you or the prior pair. Cadence is 
something you only see after the first few reps.

[rest of the welcome email]
```

**Language to the partner being re-matched away from.** Brief, no story, no blame:

```
Hi [name] — I'm re-matching [partner]. You stay in the cohort. 
You will have a new partner by [date]. Nothing is owed to me by 
way of explanation.
```

The CM never tells one partner what the other said about the re-match. Confidentiality holds across the re-match boundary.

---

## 6. The witness-partner substitute

When partners drift more than one module apart for 4+ consecutive days (Doc 04 Section I), the slower learner faces a High module without a live witness and the faster learner stalls waiting. The witness partner is the bridge.

**Who.** In priority order: a graduate of a prior cohort on the witness bench (CM maintains a small list, 2-4 people, refreshed each cohort) · a current cohort learner whose own partner is briefly off · the CM for one exchange only (last resort — compromises triage neutrality).

**When to deploy.** Cadence mismatch >1 module for 4+ days blocking the faster learner's next High module · original partner has a known temporary absence crossing a High-module window · a re-match is in progress and the new pairing has not yet built relational ground for a High module.

**What the witness partner does.** Exactly one exchange — the upcoming module's prompt, the standard three-point shape. They read the partner agreement and the module's partner-exchange prompt before recording. Not a long-term replacement; a one-rep bridge.

**Language to the learner needing the witness:**

```
Hi [name] — bringing in a witness partner for Module [N] so your 
pairing stays intact. [Witness name] is a [prior-cohort graduate / 
current-cohort learner whose partner is briefly off]. They have 
signed the agreement.

Record your Module [N] prompt and send to them on [platform]. They 
reply within 24h under the standard shape. After that, continue 
with your original partner.

Structural, not a re-match. Tell [original partner] or not — your 
call.
```

**Language to the witness partner:**

```
Hi [name] — one exchange for [learner], Module [N]. They are 
otherwise paired; partner briefly off-rhythm. Standard shape: 
receive their voice message, listen all the way through, reply 3-7 
min with what you heard / what you noticed / one question.

[Attach the Day NN partner prompt.]

Confidentiality is real. The matrix you held in your own cohort 
extends here.
```

---

## 7. High-module partner check-in script

Before unlocking a High module (Days 5, 6, 7, 9), the unlock checklist (Doc 04 Section D) requires the learner confirm *"My partner is reachable today and tomorrow."* This is not the learner asserting it in their head — it is the result of a specific exchange, 24-48 hours ahead of the module. Verbatim language the learner sends:

```
Hi [partner] — I'm about to start Module [N], a High one. Course 
rule: I confirm with you that you're reachable the next 48h before 
I unlock it.

If I send you a voice message any time in the next two days — end 
of module, during the practice, between — you'll get back within 
the 24h SLA. Same as always, just confirming.

If you can hold that — voice-reply "yes, I'm here, go." 
If you can't — also fine, just tell me. I'll wait or ask the CM 
for a witness partner. No story needed.
```

The partner replies, voice, brief: *"Yes, I'm here, go."* Or *"I can't this window, here's why."* No platform confirmation = no unlock. If the partner cannot hold it, the module waits or a witness partner is deployed (Section 6). The course will still be there in a week.

---

## 8. Closing the partnership

Day 10 closes the pairing as a course structure — explicit closure, not fade. Whatever happens after Day 10 between the learners is a different gameworld with different rules.

**The closure exchange (Day 10 partner prompt — verbatim from the module).** Each partner records 5-8 min: what you are taking forward (1-2 specific 90-day practices, not aspirational) · the declaration (one of the three Day 10 declarations, said as a declaration, out loud into the recording — partner is witness) · your sourcing (one bright principle you sourced from; one shadow principle you caught yourself sourcing from — no moralizing) · one thing you want your partner to know (gratitude, apology, question, thing left unsaid). Each replies 5-8 min: repeat the declaration verbatim into the field · what you noticed while listening · the piece of them you are carrying forward · a sentence that closes the pairing cleanly so it does not leak into ambiguity.

**Opt-in continuation.** After the closure exchange, the CM sends a private message to each partner separately:

```
Hi [name] — cohort closes [date]. The pairing as a course structure 
closes with it.

If you and [partner] want to continue beyond the cohort, that's 
between you, outside my container. I do not track post-cohort 
exchanges and do not mediate post-cohort issues.

Two things to weigh:
  - Item 7 (no sexual / financial / professional relationship) ends 
    with the cohort — no longer prohibited, also no longer 
    structurally surfaced for examination. Be deliberate.
  - The 24h SLA was structural to this course, not a promise either 
    of you owes the other for life.

Continue cleanly or close cleanly. Either is good.
```

---

## 9. Troubleshooting

The eight scenarios you will see most often, with what to do.

**1. The ghost — one partner stops responding entirely.**

After 6 days of no initiated exchange, default to a re-match for the responsive partner (Trigger 4, Section 4). Do not chase the silent partner more than twice. The silence is data; respect it. If the silent partner re-emerges later wanting to rejoin, the CM offers a witness-bench slot, not a new pairing — they re-earn matrix trust by witnessing before they are witnessed.

**2. The carrier — one partner is doing all the work.**

Voice-message the carrier privately: *"I notice you're holding more of the matrix than [partner] is right now. The pairing isn't built for that. Want me to surface it with them, or do you want to surface it yourself first?"* If the carrier wants to surface it themselves, the CM gives them the Day 8 completion-loop frame: name it cleanly, ask for what they need, close the loop. If they want the CM to surface it, the CM voice-messages the other partner with the standard cadence-drop language (Section 4, Trigger 2). Re-match if the imbalance persists past one more module.

**3. The romantic interest — one partner becomes attracted to the other.**

Item 7 forbids a sexual relationship during the course. The attraction itself is not the violation; acting on it during the cohort is. CM voice-messages the partner who surfaced the interest:

```
Hi [name] — what you noticed is real. The matrix sometimes generates 
this; you are not the first. Item 7 holds for the cohort. Notice the 
energy; do not act on it inside the course. After Day 10 you and 
[partner] decide what is between you in your own gameworld.

If the attraction makes it hard to hold a clean witnessing stance, 
tell me and I will re-match. Not punishment — choosing the matrix 
over the shape it took.
```

If mutual and announced to the CM by both, re-match both. They cannot witness each other cleanly inside an unspoken charged field. The romantic path is theirs after Day 10.

**4. The advice spiral — partner asks for advice the other can't give.**

The asking partner is bumping against a real edge. The asked partner holds the structure:

```
"What you're asking for is advice, and the agreement says I don't 
advise. What I can do is witness — tell me more about what's under 
the question. Or: this might be a CM moment, want me to flag it?"
```

If the asker keeps pushing for advice, CM voice-messages them:

```
Hi [name] — the pairing is built for witnessing, not advising. You 
keep landing on advice. That is data — either you need a different 
conversation than the pairing was built for (coach, clinician, 
referral list), or the witnessing shape is too uncomfortable to stay 
inside. Both are workable. Tell me which.
```

**5. The out-of-scope share — partner shares Red-flag material.**

Active suicidal ideation, abuse in progress, psychotic episode, severe addiction relapse — anything matching a Red flag in the triage rubric (Doc 04 Section F). The listening partner follows the buddy immediate-danger protocol (Doc 03 Section F): *"Are you in immediate danger right now?"* If yes — crisis line + CM, immediately. If no — voice-message the CM the same day. The listening partner is the relay, not the clinician.

**6. The theory debate — one partner wants to argue PM concepts.**

The pairing is not for that. The cohort feed is not for that. CM voice-messages the debater:

```
Hi [name] — the partner exchanges hold a specific shape: witness, 
reflect, ask one question. Sitting with confusion about a concept 
and voice-messaging your partner about what's hard to swallow — 
yes. Arguing whether the four levels are "really" four — different 
forum.

PM communities exist for that and I can point you. For the next 
30 days, the pairing is for the practice.
```

**7. The fixer — partner can't help advising even after being asked not to.**

The fixer is running an Old Map. The CM does not try to fix the fixer (that's the recursion they're caught in). Names the pattern once, gently:

```
Hi [name] — I heard advice came through your last exchange. Not a 
moral problem; a thoughtware one. The witnessing shape is harder 
than it sounds, especially if "helping" is how you've been useful 
your whole life. Day 8 works this directly.

Until then: in your next reply, the only three things you say back 
are "what I heard," "what I noticed," "one question." Anything 
else, leave out. Even if it feels withholding. The discomfort of 
not advising is the practice.
```

If the fixer persists past Day 8, the issue is no longer skill — it is fit. Re-match.

**8. The dropout — one partner withdraws mid-course.**

The remaining partner is re-matched (Section 5). The withdrawing partner closes via a brief CM exchange: acknowledge the choice, confirm refund/pause per cohort terms, confirm agreement items 3, 6, and 7 remain in force as honored ethics; items 1, 4, and 5 end with their cohort access. The remaining partner is told only that the partner withdrew, not why.

---

The matrix is built one exchange at a time. The CM's job is not to make the exchanges happen — that is between the partners. The CM's job is to make sure the conditions for the exchanges to happen are in place: the agreement signed, the platform set, the cadence matched, the unlock checklist gated, the silence noticed before it becomes a default. Do those, and the matrix holds. The course does the rest.

---

# §  Cohort Feed Templates

***

# Cohort Feed Templates

| | |
|---|---|
| **For** | Community Manager (CM) running the cohort feed of an async Expand the Box cohort |
| **When** | Open this file before the cohort opens; use it weekly through closure |
| **Reads alongside** | `02 - Async Delivery Framework.md` Section D · `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Sections F, H |

The cohort feed is **narrow on purpose.** Not a discussion board, not a support group, not a place for theory debate or long therapeutic confessionals — those have other homes (partner exchange, referral list, separate PM communities). The feed's one job: each learner posts a small specific signal — *I am still in the matrix, here is one thing alive in me* — and reads other learners' signals to know the cohort is alongside them.

The CM's job is to seed prompts that produce that kind of post, redirect drift toward it, and triage what shows up. Doc 04 holds the triage rubric and platform privacy minimums. This file holds the prompts and the language.

---

## 1. Cohort feed welcome post

The CM pins this at the top of the feed the day the cohort opens, before any module prompts go up. Verbatim:

```
Welcome. This is the cohort feed.

FOR:
  - One line of what landed in the module you just finished.
  - One line of what is sticking sideways.
  - Optional: one question for the group.
  - Optional: a witness offer — "if anyone needs a third party to 
    listen to something this week, I have 20 min Thursday."

NOT FOR:
  - Long processing of personal material. That goes to your partner.
  - Other people's stories.
  - Advice to other learners. The course teaches witnessing, not 
    advising. Resist the urge.
  - PM concept debate. Different forum — ask me and I'll point you.

RULES:
  - I read every post within 48h.
  - I classify in my head: GREEN (normal, no action), YELLOW (check-
    in DM within 24h), RED (active crisis — same-day response with 
    crisis line numbers in my first message).
  - Confidentiality holds; what's in the feed stays in the cohort.
  - You can delete your own posts; you can ask me to hide a post.

If a post feels too big for the feed, it probably is. Send it to 
your partner. If too big even for your partner, send it to me or 
use the referral list. The partner agreement applies here too — 
same confidentiality, same not-advising stance, same immediate-
danger protocol.

One line is enough. Often the smaller the post, the more it lands.

— [CM name]
```

---

## 2. Per-module cohort feed prompts

The CM posts one prompt to the feed at the start of each module. One or two sentences. The prompt asks for a small specific signal — never a story. Each prompt is voice-message-ready; the CM can post it as text, audio, or both.

**Day 1 — Orientation, New Context, Radical Responsibility.**

> What sentence did you choose in the red-pill ceremony? Post the sentence (not the story).

**Day 2 — Thoughtware, Thoughtmaps, Box Technology.**

> Name one move your Box made this week that you caught in the act. One sentence. (Not the story of the situation — the move itself.)

**Day 3 — Liquid State, Center-Ground-Bubble, Five Bodies.**

> Which of the five bodies is loudest in you today, and which is quietest? Two words: loud body / quiet body.

**Day 4 — Feedback, Coaching, Rapid Learning, Experiments.**

> What is one piece of feedback you received from your partner that landed somewhere unexpected? One sentence about what it landed in (the body location or the part of life). Not what they said.

**Day 5 — Feelings vs Emotions, Old Map of Feelings, Numbness Bar.**

> Name one feeling you noticed under your Numbness Bar this module. One word.

**Day 6 — Mixed Emotions and Emotional Healing Process.**

> Two-feeling combination you noticed in yourself this module. Format: "[feeling] + [feeling]." No story.

**Day 7 — Low Drama, Gremlin Food, Shifting to Responsible Game.**

> One Low Drama role you caught yourself playing this week — Victim, Persecutor, or Rescuer. One sentence on the move, not the situation. (And: did the gremlin enjoy it?)

**Day 8 — Listening, Speaking, Communication, Completion Loops.**

> Of the four Listenings, which one was hardest to hold in your Day 8 partner exchange? One word: defensive / verbatim / listening / possibility.

**Day 9 — Ego States, Problem Ownership, Learning Spiral.**

> Which ego state surfaced for you most clearly in this module's work? One word. (And: did you let it speak, or did you collapse back to a different state?)

**Day 10 — Map of Possibility, Bright Principles, Three Powers, Integration.**

> One declaration you are taking forward. (Not an intention; a declaration.)

---

## 3. What posts look like (good)

Examples the CM can hold as the shape. These are not posted as templates — they are reference for the CM's eye when triaging.

> **Day 1.** "Red pill. I am in." First time I have said something to myself I knew I meant.

> **Day 5.** Anger. Located in my jaw. I had been calling it tiredness for about six years.

> **Day 7.** Rescuer. The move was over-explaining in a work meeting so a colleague would not have to think. Gremlin loved it.

> **Day 10.** "I am the author of what my mornings become." Said it out loud to the room. Then again to my partner. Holding.

These posts share three traits: short, specific, and bring the signal back to *the learner* — not to the situation, not to other people, not to a theory.

---

## 4. What posts look like (drift)

Posts that need redirect, with the CM's verbatim DM language for each. The CM redirects privately, and may hide or delete the original depending on severity.

**Drift 1 — long therapeutic confessional.** *"My mother always told me… [600 words]… and last night my husband again did the thing where…"*

```
Hi [name] — what you posted is real material; it belongs in your 
partner exchange, not the feed. I'll hide the post (text preserved 
— I'll send it back privately if you want it). Take it to [partner] 
as your next exchange. If it's bigger than the pairing can hold, 
use the referral list.
```

**Drift 2 — advice to another learner.** *[Reply.] "I had something similar! What worked for me was…"*

```
Hi [name] — I'm hiding your reply. Not ill-intended — the feed 
isn't a place for advice between learners. The course teaches 
witnessing, not advising. What you do with the impulse: name what 
you noticed in yourself while reading their post, and say only 
that. If you want to offer a third-party witness call, the welcome 
post has the format.
```

**Drift 3 — theory debate.** *"I'm not sure I agree with the four-levels frame — in my experience the boundary between adolescent and adult is more about… [400 words]"*

```
Hi [name] — the feed isn't for theory debate. The content is fixed; 
arguing it as a cohort turns the feed into a study group, a 
different gameworld. Here is the PM community where that lives: 
[link]. I'll hide your post; repost it there if you like.

Different question: is the thing you're arguing with conceptually 
hard to sit with as practice? If yes, partner exchange.
```

**Drift 4 — witness offer that's actually advice in disguise.** *"If anyone is stuck on Day 5, I have a great technique I learned in another course I'd share over a call."*

```
Hi [name] — generous instinct. But "I'll share a technique" is 
teaching, not witnessing. A witness offer is: "if you need someone 
to listen to something for 20 min this week, I have Thursday." No 
technique, no teaching, no fixing. Repost in that format?
```

---

## 5. Cohort feed triage decision log

The CM keeps a short internal log of every post and DM, classified per the triage rubric in `04 - Container and Gatekeeping Protocol.md` Section F. The log protects the learner and the CM. It logs metadata only — the action taken — never the content of the post. Brief is fine.

Template per row:

| Date | Learner ID | Module | Post type | Flag | CM action | Follow-up date |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-02-12 | L-04 | Day 5 | Feed post | Green | None | — |
| 2026-02-12 | L-09 | Day 5 | Feed post | Yellow (stuck feeling >24h, named) | DM sent, offered voice call | 2026-02-13 |
| 2026-02-13 | L-09 | Day 5 | DM reply | Yellow (still stuck, decline call, accept stretched cadence) | Cadence adjusted, partner informed | 2026-02-15 |
| 2026-02-13 | L-11 | Day 5 | Feed post | Red (suicidal ideation, no plan named) | Crisis line numbers sent, clinician referral, cohort paused | 2026-02-14 |

The log lives in the same private spreadsheet as the pairing tracker (Doc 04 Section C), accessible only to the CM and their clinical supervisor. End-of-cohort review (Doc 04 Section L) pulls from this log.

---

## 6. Mid-course "what's alive" check-in prompt

Between Day 5 and Day 6 — after the first High module, before the most demanding one — a softer prompt that lets learners register where they are without producing material. Posted to the feed.

```
Mid-course check-in. Not a module prompt — a pause prompt.

Pick one. Post one. One sentence max.

  - The thing I came in looking for is _______ closer / further 
    away / different than I thought.
  - The body part loudest right now is _______.
  - The pace I am on is _______ right / too fast / too slow.
  - What I most want my partner to know about this week is _______.

No need to explain. I am reading.
```

The CM reads these within 24h (tighter than the normal 48h, because of mid-course intensity). Any "too fast" triggers a cadence DM. Any partner-related answer triggers a pairing-tracker check.

---

## 7. End-of-cohort gratitude prompts

After Day 10. Two posts the CM seeds.

**Partner-to-partner (learners reply tagging their partner).**

```
Pairings closed today. Cohort closes this week.

If you want to thank your partner publicly, this is the post. One 
or two sentences. Tag them. Specific is better than generic — what 
you carry forward FROM them, not "thanks for being amazing."

Thanking them in private only is also clean. The public version 
lets the cohort witness that the matrix held.
```

**Partner-to-cohort (CM seeds the next day, learners reply).**

```
Last post on this feed.

If you want to say one thing to the cohort — not to a person, to 
the room — say it here. The room held you while you held your 
partner while your partner held you. That circulation is the 
cohort.

One line. What you take with you. What you are leaving here.

Feed closes for posting [date, 7 days out], archived read-only for 
[duration]. Pairing continuation (if any) is between you and your 
partner; the cohort as a structure ends here.

Thank you for being in this matrix.

— [CM name]
```

After the gratitude window, the CM runs the post-cohort review (Doc 04 Section L).

---

The feed is small on purpose. Twelve good one-line posts per module is healthy. Three long posts per module is the feed pulling toward the wrong attractor — fix the prompts, fix the redirects, fix the welcome post if drift is persistent. Signal-to-noise on the feed is the CM's clearest read on whether the cohort is using the matrix or substituting the feed for it.

---

# §  Solo Centering and Grounding Scripts

***

# Solo Centering and Grounding Scripts

> A library of script-ready solo practices for the learner. Read once. Then use.

---

## When to use this file

This file is for you, the learner. It contains eleven scripts. Some are 60 seconds — for when you need to come back into your body in the middle of a module and decide what to do next. Some are 12 minutes — the standard energetic-body practice you will run before every High module from Day 5 onwards. Some are emergency scripts for the specific things that happen: crying that won't stop, going numb, the disorientation of liquid state, the over-stimulated nervous system at the end of a processing day.

None of these are meditations. They are PM practices. They install distinctions through the body — center, ground, bubble, cube, the four feelings as energies, the difference between feeling and dissociating — and they are most useful when run as scripts you read aloud (or record once and play back) rather than as ideas you "do in your head." Doing them in your head is the Box's performance of doing them.

**How to use this file:**
- Bookmark it. You will reach for it more in Weeks 2–4 of the course than in Week 1.
- Record the ones you use most as voice memos on your phone. Your own voice reading these to you is more useful than reading silently mid-state.
- Run them as written before you customize. Run as written for 30 days. Then adapt if you must.
- Share scripts 2 and 7–10 with your pairing partner — those are the ones a partner may need to talk you through over voice message if you are flooded.
- These scripts do not replace the safety pathway in Doc 03. If you are in crisis, ground first, then reach the buddy and the CM. The scripts are the *first move*, not the only move.

The 60-second universal grounding script is reproduced from Doc 03 Section D for use anywhere — including for sharing on the cohort feed when you want to ask the cohort to ground with you. The other ten scripts are new and live only here.

---

## 1. The 60-second universal grounding script

This is the script. The one at the top of every module. The default action whenever you notice you have gone far away from yourself.

> **Grounding (60 seconds).**
>
> 1. Stop whatever you were doing in the module. Close the video or the document.
> 2. Stand up. Both feet on the floor. Knees soft.
> 3. Breathe out longer than you breathe in, three times. Audible exhale is fine.
> 4. Name three things you can see in the room.
> 5. Name one thing you can hear.
> 6. Place one hand on your sternum, the other on your belly. Notice that your body is here.
> 7. When you have come back, decide: continue, pause for 10 minutes, or stop the module for today.

Use this any time you notice:
- Feeling far away from yourself
- Inability to follow the words on the page or in the video
- Heart racing without clear cause
- Watching yourself from outside
- Crying that does not feel clean — feels stuck
- Strong urge to flee, attack, or shut down

These are nervous-system signals, not signs something is wrong with you. Ground first. Decide second.

---

## 2. The 5-minute centering practice

For the start of every module. Run it before you open the file. It is the difference between the module landing in your body and the module landing in your head as content.

> **Script. 5 minutes. Read aloud or play back. Eyes open or closed — your choice.**
>
> **Minute 1 — arrive.** Sit. Both feet on the floor. Spine upright but not braced. Shoulders down. Hands resting on your thighs or in your lap.
>
> Three breaths. Each exhale longer than the inhale. Make the exhale audible on at least one.
>
> Notice the chair under you. Notice the floor under your feet. Notice the temperature of the air on your face.
>
> **Minute 2 — find your center.** Move your attention to your lower belly — a hand's-width below your navel, behind the abdominal wall. This is the hara. For most people, this is where your center actually lives.
>
> Say out loud, or in your head if you need to: *"My center is here."*
>
> If your attention drifts to your head — to thoughts, to planning, to the day — notice. Bring it back to your belly. The drift is not a problem. The noticing-and-returning is the practice.
>
> If your center is not in your belly — if it actually lives behind your sternum, in your heart — locate it there. Where it actually is.
>
> **Minute 3 — drop a grounding cord.** From your center, declare a thick energetic cord — ship's-rope diameter — going down through your seat, through the floor, through the building, into the earth, all the way to the center.
>
> Say out loud: *"My grounding cord is dropped."*
>
> Not visualization. Declaration. It exists because you said so.
>
> Let excess energy drain. Tension from your day. Charge from the conversation you just had. The buzz of the screens. Allow. Do not push.
>
> **Minute 4 — set a bubble.** Declare a sphere of energy around you. Arm's length in every direction. Under your feet. Above your head.
>
> Say out loud: *"My bubble is set."*
>
> Inside the bubble: your body, your breath, your feelings, your rhythm, this module. Outside the bubble: the room beyond arm's length, the street noise, the partner you were thinking about, the email you have not answered. Real, *not yours, not right now*.
>
> If the bubble feels too big — pull it in. Too small or collapsed — push it out. Your choice.
>
> **Minute 5 — hold all three and arrive.** Center. Grounding cord. Bubble.
>
> Three breaths. Slow. Audible exhale.
>
> Now, out loud: *"I am here. I am centered. I am grounded. I am bubbled. I am ready to begin the module."*
>
> Open the document. Begin.

Run this before every module. Every single one. Including the Low intensity ones. By Module 4 it will take you 90 seconds because the equipment is yours; until then, run all five minutes.

---

## 3. Center + grounding cord + bubble — the standard practice (10 minutes)

This is the longer-form version of Practice 2. Run it once a day during the course if you can, and always before any High module (5, 6, 7, 9) — that is what the consent check is referring to when it says *"I know how to ground."*

> **Script. 10 minutes. Chair, water, no phone, no music. Read it through once, then run it.**
>
> **Minute 1 — settle.** Sit. Both feet on the floor. Drink water. Three audible exhales.
>
> Notice three things you can see. One thing you can hear. The temperature of your hands.
>
> **Minutes 2–3 — find center.** Move attention to the lower belly. Hand's-width below the navel, behind the abdominal wall.
>
> *"My center is here."*
>
> Stay there. Attention will drift up — to head, to thought, to plan. Each time you notice the drift, return. The rep is *noticing and returning*, not staying.
>
> If your center actually lives in your heart (some people, particularly artists and healers, do live there), locate it where it actually is. Trust where your body says it is.
>
> Place one hand on your center. Feel the rise and fall of breath through the hand. Sixty seconds.
>
> **Minutes 4–5 — drop the grounding cord.** From your center, declare a thick cord. Ship's-rope diameter. Down through your seat, through the floor, through whatever is beneath the floor, into the earth, into the bedrock, all the way to the core of the planet.
>
> *"My grounding cord is dropped."*
>
> Notice if your cord wants to be a different size or material. Some people's cord is a tree trunk; some, a column of light; some, a steel cable. Do not pick. Notice what it actually is.
>
> Let excess discharge. Energy that is not yours — what you absorbed from the last conversation, the news, the city — drains down the cord. Do not push it. Allow.
>
> Notice colour, weight, temperature in the cord. Do not interpret. Just note.
>
> **Minutes 6–7 — set the bubble.** Declare a sphere of energy around your body. Arm's length in every direction. Under your feet, above your head, behind you.
>
> *"My bubble is set."*
>
> Walk the perimeter of the bubble with your attention. Right. Behind. Left. Front. Above. Below. The edges are where your body's "yours" meets the world's "not yours."
>
> Notice the size. Too big — your energy is stretched thin, you are leaking into the room. Pull it in. Too small or collapsed — you are squeezed, you have given your space away to whoever or whatever is in your head. Push it out to arm's length.
>
> Inside: body, breath, feelings, rhythm, this practice. Outside: real, *not yours*.
>
> **Minutes 8–9 — hold all three.** Center. Cord. Bubble.
>
> Three slow breaths.
>
> Body scan, fast. Top of head — present? Throat — present? Heart — present? Hands — present? Belly — present? Pelvis — present? Legs — present? Feet — present? Note where you are clearly here and where you are still partly somewhere else. Do not fix it. Notice.
>
> **Minute 10 — choose.** What is next?
>
> If you are entering a module: *"I am centered, grounded, bubbled. I am beginning the module."*
>
> If you are entering a conversation: *"I am centered, grounded, bubbled. I am entering this conversation."*
>
> If you are entering sleep: *"I am centered, grounded, bubbled. I am letting the day complete."*
>
> Drink water. Stand up. Go.

The equipment compounds. By the third or fourth pass it is yours and you can run it in 60 seconds when you need to. Until then — full ten minutes. The reps build the perceptual interface.

---

## 4. The golden cube — workspace setup (12 minutes)

Run this when you are about to declare something or run a specific experiment in your actual life that the module surfaced. The golden cube is the energetic workspace inside which you place one piece of thoughtware work — a distinction to land, a piece of your Box to look at, a declaration to test, an experiment to design.

Not for daily use. For when there is something to construct or test.

> **Script. 12 minutes. Chair, water, notebook open. Read aloud or record.**
>
> **Minutes 1–4 — center, ground, bubble.** Run the practice from Script 3, shortened. Center. Cord. Bubble. Three breaths.
>
> Confirm: *"I am centered. I am grounded. I am bubbled."*
>
> Do not open the cube until the three are stable. If they are not stable, run Script 3 in full first.
>
> **Minute 5 — open the cube.** Two paces in front of you, declare a cube of golden light. Size of a small room — large enough to walk into if you wanted to, though you will not. Edges crisp. The interior is a workspace.
>
> *"The cube is open."*
>
> Notice the cube. Notice that it is two paces away, not on top of you, not inside you. The distance is the point. You are looking at it. You are not in it.
>
> **Minutes 6–7 — place the work inside.** Decide what you are placing inside the cube. **One piece only.** Common pieces:
> - A distinction you are trying to land (*"feeling vs. emotion in my relationship with my brother"*)
> - A piece of your Box you want to look at from outside (*"the rule that says I do not raise my voice"*)
> - A situation this week you are about to walk into (*"the conversation with my boss tomorrow"*)
> - A declaration you are considering (*"I am running the daily box catch for 30 days"*)
> - An experiment you are designing (*what / by when / what I will notice*)
>
> Say out loud what you are placing inside: *"I am placing inside the cube: [the piece]."*
>
> See it inside the cube. As a sentence, as a shape, as a memory, as a phrase. However your body wants to put it there.
>
> **Minutes 8–10 — look.** Stay centered, grounded, bubbled. Eyes soft. Attention on the cube.
>
> Do not solve. Do not figure out. Do not plan.
>
> Look.
>
> Notice what becomes visible about the piece that was not visible before you put it in the cube. Often: where the Box is hiding inside the piece. What ego state is running the piece. What feeling is underneath. What declaration would change everything. What experiment would test the smallest version.
>
> Do not write yet. Look. Two to three minutes.
>
> **Minute 11 — capture.** Open your notebook. Write fast, no editing. One to three sentences:
> - What became visible inside the cube
> - What the next move is — declaration, experiment, conversation, pause
> - What you are not yet ready to do
>
> Close the notebook.
>
> **Minute 12 — close the cube.** Out loud: *"The cube is closed."*
>
> The cube dissolves. The work stays.
>
> Confirm: *"I am centered. I am grounded. I am bubbled."*
>
> Three breaths. Drink water. Stand up. Go.

The cube is a workspace, not a refuge. Opened to construct or test. Closed when done. A learner who walks around with the cube permanently open is leaking — close it.

---

## 5. The dissolution script (8 minutes)

Run this at the end of any High module — Day 5, 6, 7, or 9 — to clear residue from the practice. The emotional body has been worked. The energetic body has held a charged container. Both want clearing before you return to ordinary life. Without this, you carry the module's residue into the next conversation, the next meal, the next sleep — and call that residue your mood.

> **Script. 8 minutes. Standing if you can, sitting if you must. Notebook open at the end.**
>
> **Minute 1 — confirm equipment.** Stand. Both feet on the floor. Center. Grounding cord. Bubble.
>
> Confirm out loud: *"I am centered. I am grounded. I am bubbled."*
>
> Three audible exhales.
>
> **Minute 2 — name what was worked.** Out loud, in one sentence: *"In this module, I worked [the piece]. What surfaced was [the feeling or material]."*
>
> Naming completes the practice. Until named, the practice has not finished.
>
> **Minutes 3–4 — discharge through the cord.** Bring attention to your center. Then to the cord.
>
> Out loud: *"Anything that is not mine, drain."*
>
> Feel — or imagine until you feel — the cord widening. Whatever you absorbed from the practice that is not yours moves down. Old emotional charge that surfaced and was not yet ready to process. The residue of your Box's noise. Tension in shoulders, jaw, gut. Allow.
>
> Sixty seconds, eyes soft, do nothing but allow.
>
> **Minute 5 — release the bubble's content.** The bubble has been the container for the practice. Now release its content.
>
> Out loud: *"Whatever entered my bubble in this practice that is not mine, leaves."*
>
> Imagine — or know — your bubble's edges becoming briefly permeable, then re-sealing. What was witness energy from your partner's earlier message, what was charge from the video, what was your Box's commentary — all releases.
>
> *"My bubble is set."* Re-confirm.
>
> **Minute 6 — physical movement.** Move the body. Shake hands and arms loosely for 30 seconds. Roll shoulders. Roll neck once each direction. Stretch jaw — yawn audibly, twice. Stamp feet ten times.
>
> Stored energy that did not move during the practice leaves now. The body completes what the practice started.
>
> **Minute 7 — drink and re-orient.** Drink a full glass of water, slowly. Cold water is fine. Hot water is fine.
>
> Look around the room. Name three things out loud. *"I see the lamp. I see the chair. I see the door."*
>
> Name what time of day it is. Name what you are about to do next.
>
> **Minute 8 — capture and close.** Notebook open. Write three lines, fast:
> - What I worked: ___
> - What surfaced: ___
> - What I am leaving in the practice (not carrying into the rest of the day): ___
>
> Close the notebook. Out loud: *"The practice is complete."*
>
> Walk away. The work is done. Trust that what wants to integrate will integrate while you do other things. Do not chew on it.

Run this after every High module. Skipping it is what makes Day 5 still being processed on Day 8. Run it.

---

## 6. The "I started crying and can't stop" emergency script (3 minutes)

Use the moment you notice the crying is not coming in waves with arrival, peak, and dissipation — it is looping, falling, or feels like there is no exit. This is emotion (per Day 5), not present-time sadness. The container needs to shift.

> **Script. 3 minutes. Read it aloud to yourself between sobs if you have to.**
>
> **Step 1 — interrupt.** Out loud: *"Stop."* Or: *"Pause."* Whatever word your body responds to.
>
> Stand up. If you cannot stand, sit upright and put both feet flat on the floor.
>
> **Step 2 — water on the face.** Get to the sink. Cold water — splash on your face. Once. Twice. Three times. The cold shocks the vagus nerve and resets the cry response. This is physiological, not punishment.
>
> Look in the mirror. See your own eyes for two seconds.
>
> **Step 3 — five senses.** Name out loud:
> - Five things you can see *("the mirror, the tap, the tile, my hand, the towel")*
> - Four things you can hear *("the tap dripping, my breath, the fridge, traffic")*
> - Three things you can feel *("water on my face, floor under my feet, the towel in my hand")*
> - Two things you can smell *("the soap, my own skin")*
> - One thing you can taste *("the inside of my mouth")*
>
> The crying will slow or stop during this. If it does not, repeat the five senses naming once more.
>
> **Step 4 — locate the emotion, do not process it.** Sit down. Put one hand on your chest, one on your belly.
>
> Out loud: *"This is an emotion. Not a present-time feeling. I am not processing it right now."*
>
> Name what age it might be from, if anything comes: *"This is old. This is from [a time, an age, a memory]."*
>
> Do not story. Do not figure out. Naming and stopping is the move.
>
> **Step 5 — partner message, then choose.** Pick up the phone. Voice message your pairing partner. Short: *"I hit an emotion in the module. I am grounded. I stopped. I am okay. I am letting you know."*
>
> Then decide:
> - Stop the module for today. Re-enter tomorrow.
> - If the crying restarts, run this script again, and message the CM.
> - If you have a therapist, this is a clean time to use a session. Be specific: *"I am doing a feelings-vs-emotions module. I hit an emotion. I am grounded. Can we work with it?"*
>
> Drink water. Move your body for two minutes — walk to another room, look out a window. Do not return to the module today.

The crying that loops is an open wound waiting for the right conditions to close. The right conditions are *not* finishing this module today. The right conditions are: ground, witness, professional support if needed, time. The course will be here tomorrow.

---

## 7. The "I went numb" emergency script (3 minutes)

Different shape from crying that won't stop. Numbness shows up as: you cannot feel anything in your body. You are watching the module from outside yourself. The words on the page are not landing. You notice you have stopped breathing fully. You feel a flatness that is somehow louder than feelings.

This is the Box re-installing the Numbness Bar in real time, because the previous practice loosened it. Numbness is information.

> **Script. 3 minutes.**
>
> **Step 1 — name it.** Out loud: *"I have gone numb. This is the Numbness Bar."*
>
> Naming brings consciousness to it. Without naming, you stay underneath.
>
> **Step 2 — move physically, hard.** Numbness will not lift from sitting still and trying to feel.
>
> Stand. Stamp your feet, hard, ten times. Hear the stamp.
>
> Press your palms together as hard as you can for ten seconds. Feel the resistance.
>
> Push against a wall — both hands flat against the wall, lean in, push with your legs, twenty seconds. Feel the muscles in your arms, shoulders, legs.
>
> Numbness lifts through pressure, not through softness.
>
> **Step 3 — find one sensation.** Sit back down. Center, ground, bubble — fast version.
>
> Pick one body location. Hands. Just your hands. Look at them.
>
> Out loud: *"In my hands right now, the sensation is [warm / cold / tingling / heavy / nothing yet — say nothing yet if that is what is true]."*
>
> If you found a sensation, locate one more — feet, or jaw, or chest. Name it.
>
> If you still feel nothing — drink cold water. Touch something with a sharp temperature. Hold an ice cube if you have one. Feel the cold. *Name the cold out loud.*
>
> **Step 4 — find one feeling at 2%.** Now, much smaller: *"In my emotional body, right now, at 2%, is there some anger, sadness, fear, or joy?"*
>
> Take whatever comes. *"Some fear, 2%, in my chest."* Or *"Some sadness, 3%, behind my eyes."* The 2% is enough. Do not chase a bigger version.
>
> If nothing comes after sixty seconds — that is data. Note it. The Numbness Bar is high today. That is information, not failure.
>
> **Step 5 — partner message, then decide.** Voice message your partner: *"I went numb in the module. I am grounded. I stopped. I will re-enter tomorrow."*
>
> Decide: stop the module today. Do something physical and grounding for an hour — walk outside, cook a real meal, take a hot shower, talk to another human about something unrelated. Numbness lifts through ordinary embodied life, not through more module.
>
> Re-enter the module tomorrow with Script 2 first.

Numbness is not failure. The Box did its old job — it cut the signal because the signal was going to be more than the system thought it could handle. You teach the system, slowly, that the signal is workable. The teaching is the work.

---

## 8. The "I'm in liquid state and don't know who I am" reorientation script (5 minutes)

The disorientation that arises mid-course is real, and it is normal. The Box has loosened enough that the old answer to *who am I* is not snapping back into place. The new answer has not formed yet. You are between thoughtwares. The feeling can be unmistakable — *I don't know what I think about anything anymore* — and is often confused for crisis. It is not crisis. It is liquid state. It is exactly what the course is for.

But you need to walk while you are in it, and walking requires equipment.

> **Script. 5 minutes.**
>
> **Minute 1 — name the state.** Out loud: *"I am in liquid state. This is not crisis. The old thoughtware is loose. The new thoughtware has not stabilized yet. This is what the course is for."*
>
> Naming relocates the disorientation from *something wrong with me* to *the predictable consequence of the work I am doing*.
>
> **Minute 2 — center, ground, bubble.** Fast version. Stand if you can.
>
> Center — hand on lower belly. *"My center is here."*
>
> Cord — *"My grounding cord is dropped."*
>
> Bubble — *"My bubble is set."*
>
> Three breaths.
>
> The equipment is what lets you stay in liquid state without flooding. Without the equipment, liquid state destabilizes. With it, liquid state works.
>
> **Minute 3 — what is still true.** Out loud, list what is still true. Things that have not become uncertain.
>
> *"My name is ___. I live in ___. The people I love today are ___. The work I do is ___. The body I am in is mine. The date is ___. I am taking the Expand the Box course and I am on Day ___."*
>
> If some of those are also currently in question, say only the ones that are not.
>
> The point is: there is a floor. The floor did not disappear. The Box was claiming credit for the floor — when the Box loosens, it feels like the floor is going too. It is not. Find the floor.
>
> **Minute 4 — what is in flux.** Out loud, name what is in flux. *"What is in flux right now is [my certainty about my job / my story about my marriage / my picture of who I am at work / my relationship with my parents]."*
>
> Naming it as flux distinguishes it from collapse. Flux is movement. Collapse is the absence of structure.
>
> *"This is liquid state in [the area]. I am letting the old thoughtware loosen. I am not yet rebuilding the new."*
>
> **Minute 5 — choose the next small thing.** Liquid state is not the time for large decisions. The decisions made in liquid state, sourced from disorientation, are usually the Box trying to grab any thoughtware to stop the discomfort of having none.
>
> Out loud: *"I will not make any large decisions in the next 48 hours. I will not quit, leave, end, or commit. I will pause."*
>
> Then choose **one** small concrete next thing. Drink water. Eat a meal. Walk for 20 minutes. Voice-message my partner. Sleep.
>
> Do that small thing. Then the next small thing. The thoughtware reformation happens on its own — your job is not to construct it on the spot. Your job is to *be alive while it happens*.

If the disorientation persists for more than 48 hours and does not respond to grounding, contact the CM. There is a difference between liquid state (workable with equipment) and a state that has spilled past what the course can hold (needs professional support). The CM helps you tell which.

---

## 9. Pre-sleep grounding for processing days (4 minutes)

Run this on the evening of any High module day, before you get into bed. The emotional and energetic body have been worked; sleep is when integration happens, but only if the system is not still spinning. This script signals to the system: *the work is complete for today, you may sleep now*.

> **Script. 4 minutes. Sitting on the edge of the bed, lights dim, phone away.**
>
> **Minute 1 — settle the room.** Put your phone in another room or face-down on do-not-disturb. Lights low. Water by the bed.
>
> Sit on the edge of the bed. Both feet on the floor.
>
> Three audible exhales, each longer than the inhale. Make them slow.
>
> **Minute 2 — center, ground, bubble.** Fast version, lying-down-ready.
>
> Center — hand on belly. *"My center is here."*
>
> Cord — *"My grounding cord is dropped. Anything that is not mine drains."*
>
> Bubble — *"My bubble is set. The day is outside it. The bedroom is the size of my bubble."*
>
> **Minute 3 — close the day.** Out loud, in one sentence each:
> - What I worked today: *"Today I worked [Day __, the practice, the partner exchange]."*
> - What surfaced: *"What surfaced was [the feeling / the realization / the question]."*
> - What is incomplete: *"What is incomplete and waiting is [name it, do not solve it]."*
> - What I am setting down for sleep: *"I am setting down [the worry, the conversation, the loop]. It will be there in the morning if it matters. I am letting sleep do its work."*
>
> Naming closes the loop. Unnamed loops keep running through the night.
>
> **Minute 4 — release the cord and rest.** Out loud: *"The work for today is complete."*
>
> Lie down. Feel the bed under you — full length of your body. Hands resting at your sides or on your belly.
>
> Center is still here. Grounding cord is still dropped — it does not turn off for sleep. Bubble is the size of the bed.
>
> Three slow breaths. Do not try to sleep. Let sleep come.
>
> If thought-loops start — name them: *"That is thought. I am not following it tonight."* Return attention to the cord, to the belly, to the breath.

The integration that happens in sleep after a processing day is real and large. The system is metabolizing what the module loosened. Protect the sleep — no scrolling, no late drink, no late food, no opening one more email. The pre-sleep ground is the move that says: *the day is closed; the integration can begin*.

---

## 10. Grounding outdoors (walking or sitting in nature)

Same principles, adapted for outside. Use when you are walking on processing days, or when you have stepped outside between module sections to clear your head. Many learners report the outdoor version is faster than indoor because the body is already in motion and the senses are already engaged.

> **Script. Variable length — works at 3 minutes or 30. Read it once, then go.**
>
> **First — choose your spot or your path.** A park. A street. A trail. A garden. Even a city block. The outdoor is what matters; it does not need to be wild.
>
> Phone in pocket, on silent. No earbuds. The point is to listen with the body.
>
> **Settle into the body.** Stand for thirty seconds. Both feet on the ground (or earth, or pavement — it works on pavement). Notice the contact through the soles.
>
> Three audible exhales.
>
> **Find your center while standing.** Hand on lower belly. *"My center is here."*
>
> Notice that center can be found while standing, while walking, anywhere. The Box wants to convince you grounding is only for sitting with eyes closed. It is not.
>
> **Drop a grounding cord through the ground.** *"My grounding cord is dropped."*
>
> The cord goes through the ground or pavement, through whatever is under it, into the earth. Pavement does not break it. The cord exists because you said so.
>
> Walking with a dropped cord feels different from walking without one. You will feel the difference in 30–60 seconds — a kind of weight in the lower body that was not there before, a steadiness.
>
> **Set the bubble — outdoors size.** Out loud or in your head: *"My bubble is set, arm's length."*
>
> Outdoors the bubble is the same size as indoors. Resist the pull to make it bigger because you are in open space. Arm's length keeps it operational.
>
> **Begin walking, or sit if you are sitting.** Now use the senses.
>
> *Three things you can see, named in your head as you walk: "tree, fence, sky."*
>
> *Two things you can hear: "bird, car."*
>
> *One thing you can smell: "grass, wet pavement, rain."*
>
> If you are walking, match your breath to your stride for a few minutes. Inhale three steps, exhale four. Find the count your body wants.
>
> **Notice the feeling in the body.** *"In my emotional body, right now, at low intensity, is there some anger, sadness, fear, joy?"*
>
> Outdoors, feelings often arrive that have been blocked indoors. The open space gives them room. Name what arrives, locate it, do not story it. Keep walking.
>
> **Close when you return.** Before you come back inside, pause at the door. *"I am centered. I am grounded. I am bubbled. I am returning indoors."*
>
> If you sat — same close, before you stand to leave.

The outdoor practice does not replace the indoor one. It runs alongside it. The combination — daily indoor practice plus regular outdoor grounding — is what installs the energetic-body equipment most reliably across the 30 days of the course and the 90 days after.

---

## 11. Final note

These eleven scripts are the equipment. You do not have to do all of them every day. You have to know which one to reach for in the moment you need it.

Three rules:

1. **Run as written before you customize.** The scripts have been tuned. They land cleanly if read as written. Customizations are best made after 30 days of as-written practice, not before.
2. **Read them aloud or record them.** PM is a body practice. Scripts read silently land in the head. Scripts read aloud — or played back in your own voice — land in the body. The difference is large.
3. **Do not skip the practice because you are "fine."** *Fine* is often the Box. The practice is the rep. The rep is the work.

When you come back to this file in Week 4, you will find some of the scripts you needed in Week 2 you no longer need — the equipment has installed. New scripts (3, 4, 5) will be the ones you use most. That is the arc.

Welcome to your own equipment.

---
